P1 Taylor 3rd Order — Newton's Cooling

A metal rod cools according to Newton's law: \( \dfrac{dT}{dt} = -2(T - 20) \),   \( T(0) = 100°C \).

Using the 3rd order Taylor method with \( h = 0.1 \) s, find \( T(0.5) \).

Hints: \( f = -2(T-20) \), compute \( y'' \) and \( y''' \) analytically first.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

\[ \frac{dT}{dt}=-2(T-20), \qquad T(0)=100 \]

Third-order Taylor method:

\[ T_{n+1}=T_n+hT'_n+\frac{h^2}{2}T''_n+\frac{h^3}{6}T'''_n \]

Derivative Calculations

\[ T'=-2(T-20) \] \[ T''=-2T'=4(T-20) \] \[ T'''=-2T''=-8(T-20) \] With \(h=0.1\), \[ T_{n+1} = T_n +0.1[-2(T_n-20)] +\frac{0.01}{2}[4(T_n-20)] +\frac{0.001}{6}[-8(T_n-20)] \] \[ T_{n+1} = T_n-0.181333(T_n-20) \]

Step 1: \(t=0\rightarrow0.1\)

\[ T_0=100 \] \[ T'_0=-2(100-20)=-160 \] \[ T''_0=4(100-20)=320 \] \[ T'''_0=-8(100-20)=-640 \] \[ T_1 = 100+0.1(-160)+\frac{0.01}{2}(320)+\frac{0.001}{6}(-640) \] \[ T_1 = 100-16+1.6-0.106667 \] \[ T_1=85.493333 \]

Step 2: \(t=0.1\rightarrow0.2\)

\[ T'_1=-2(85.493333-20)=-130.986667 \] \[ T''_1=261.973333 \] \[ T'''_1=-523.946667 \] \[ T_2 = 85.493333 +0.1(-130.986667) +\frac{0.01}{2}(261.973333) +\frac{0.001}{6}(-523.946667) \] \[ T_2=73.617209 \]

Step 3: \(t=0.2\rightarrow0.3\)

\[ T'_2=-107.234418 \] \[ T''_2=214.468836 \] \[ T'''_2=-428.937671 \] \[ T_3 = 73.617209 +0.1(-107.234418) +\frac{0.01}{2}(214.468836) +\frac{0.001}{6}(-428.937671) \] \[ T_3=63.894622 \]

Step 4: \(t=0.3\rightarrow0.4\)

\[ T'_3=-87.789243 \] \[ T''_3=175.578487 \] \[ T'''_3=-351.156973 \] \[ T_4=55.935064 \]

Step 5: \(t=0.4\rightarrow0.5\)

\[ T'_4=-71.870127 \] \[ T''_4=143.740254 \] \[ T'''_4=-287.480509 \] \[ T_5 = 55.935064 +0.1(-71.870127) +\frac{0.01}{2}(143.740254) +\frac{0.001}{6}(-287.480509) \] \[ \boxed{T(0.5)=49.418839^\circ C} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P1 Taylor 3rd Order

Newton's Cooling — Taylor 3rd Order
%% P1 — Taylor 3rd Order Method: Newton's Cooling
      
      clc;
      clear;
      close all;
      
      % Problem data
      h = 0.1;
      t0 = 0;
      tf = 0.5;
      T0 = 100;
      
      t = t0:h:tf;
      N = length(t);
      
      T = zeros(1, N);
      T(1) = T0;
      
      % Derivatives:
      % T'   = -2(T - 20)
      % T''  =  4(T - 20)
      % T''' = -8(T - 20)
      
      for n = 1:N-1
      
          Tp   = -2*(T(n) - 20);
          Tpp  =  4*(T(n) - 20);
          Tppp = -8*(T(n) - 20);
      
          T(n+1) = T(n) ...
              + h*Tp ...
              + (h^2/2)*Tpp ...
              + (h^3/6)*Tppp;
      
      end
      
      Exact = 20 + 80*exp(-2*t);
      Error = abs(Exact - T);
      
      Results = table(t', T', Exact', Error', ...
          'VariableNames', {'t', 'Taylor3_T', 'Exact_T', 'Abs_Error'});
      
      disp(Results)
      
      fprintf('T(0.5) = %.6f C\n', T(end))
P2 RK2 Heun — Linear Decay with Forcing

Solve \( \dfrac{dC}{dt} = -C + \sin(t) \),   \( C(0) = 1 \), with Heun's method, \( h = 0.1 \).

Find \( C(0.5) \). Compare with the exact solution (integrating factor gives \( C = 2e^{-t} + \tfrac{\sin t - \cos t}{2} + \tfrac{1}{2}e^{-t} \)).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

\[ \frac{dC}{dt}=-C+\sin(t), \qquad C(0)=1 \]

Heun's Method (RK2)

\[ k_1=f(t_n,C_n) \] \[ C^*=C_n+hk_1 \] \[ k_2=f(t_n+h,C^*) \] \[ C_{n+1} = C_n+\frac{h}{2}(k_1+k_2) \]

Use \(h=0.1\).

Step 1: \(t=0\rightarrow0.1\)

\[ C_0=1 \] \[ k_1=-1+\sin(0)=-1 \] \[ C^*=1+0.1(-1)=0.9 \] \[ k_2=-0.9+\sin(0.1) \] \[ k_2=-0.80016658 \] \[ C_1 = 1+\frac{0.1}{2} (-1-0.80016658) \] \[ C_1=0.90999167 \]

Step 2: \(t=0.1\rightarrow0.2\)

\[ k_1 = -0.90999167+\sin(0.1) = -0.81015825 \] \[ C^* = 0.90999167 +0.1(-0.81015825) = 0.82897585 \] \[ k_2 = -0.82897585+\sin(0.2) = -0.63030651 \] \[ C_2 = 0.90999167 +0.05(-0.81015825-0.63030651) \] \[ C_2=0.83796843 \]

Step 3: \(t=0.2\rightarrow0.3\)

\[ k_1=-0.63929910 \] \[ C^*=0.77403852 \] \[ k_2=-0.47851832 \] \[ C_3=0.78207756 \]

Step 4: \(t=0.3\rightarrow0.4\)

\[ k_1=-0.48655735 \] \[ C^*=0.73342183 \] \[ k_2=-0.34400348 \] \[ C_4=0.74054952 \]

Step 5: \(t=0.4\rightarrow0.5\)

\[ k_1=-0.35113118 \] \[ C^*=0.70543640 \] \[ k_2=-0.22601086 \] \[ C_5 = 0.74054952 +0.05(-0.35113118-0.22601086) \] \[ \boxed{C(0.5)=0.71169242} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P2 RK2 Heun

Linear Decay with Forcing — Heun Method
%% P2 — RK2 Heun Method
      
      clc;
      clear;
      close all;
      
      h = 0.1;
      t0 = 0;
      tf = 0.5;
      C0 = 1;
      
      t = t0:h:tf;
      N = length(t);
      
      C = zeros(1, N);
      C(1) = C0;
      
      f = @(t,C) -C + sin(t);
      
      k1 = zeros(1, N-1);
      k2 = zeros(1, N-1);
      Cpred = zeros(1, N-1);
      
      for n = 1:N-1
      
          k1(n) = f(t(n), C(n));
      
          Cpred(n) = C(n) + h*k1(n);
      
          k2(n) = f(t(n) + h, Cpred(n));
      
          C(n+1) = C(n) + (h/2)*(k1(n) + k2(n));
      
      end
      
      % Exact solution from integrating factor
      Exact = 0.5*(sin(t) - cos(t)) + 1.5*exp(-t);
      
      Error = abs(Exact - C);
      
      Results = table(t', C', Exact', Error', ...
          'VariableNames', {'t', 'Heun_C', 'Exact_C', 'Abs_Error'});
      
      disp(Results)
      
      fprintf('C(0.5) = %.6f\n', C(end))
P3 RK4 — Michaelis-Menten Enzyme Kinetics

Substrate consumption in an enzyme reactor:

\[ \frac{dS}{dt} = -\frac{V_{max} S}{K_m + S}, \quad V_{max} = 2\;\tfrac{mol}{L\cdot s},\quad K_m = 1\;\tfrac{mol}{L}, \quad S(0) = 5\;\tfrac{mol}{L} \]

Use RK4 with \( h = 0.1 \) s to find \( S(0.5) \). This is a single step.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

\[ \frac{dS}{dt} = -\frac{2S}{1+S} \] \[ S(0)=5 \] \[ h=0.1 \]

Classical RK4 Formula:

\[ k_1=f(t_n,S_n) \] \[ k_2=f\left(t_n+\frac h2, S_n+\frac h2k_1\right) \] \[ k_3=f\left(t_n+\frac h2, S_n+\frac h2k_2\right) \] \[ k_4=f(t_n+h,S_n+hk_3) \] \[ S_{n+1} = S_n + \frac h6 \left( k_1+2k_2+2k_3+k_4 \right) \]

Step 1 : \(t=0 \rightarrow 0.1\)

\[ S_0=5 \] \[ k_1 = -\frac{2(5)}{1+5} = -1.666667 \] \[ k_2 = -\frac{2(5+0.05k_1)} {1+(5+0.05k_1)} \] \[ = -\frac{2(4.916667)} {5.916667} \] \[ k_2=-1.662921 \] \[ k_3 = -\frac{2(5+0.05k_2)} {1+(5+0.05k_2)} \] \[ = -\frac{2(4.916854)} {5.916854} \] \[ k_3=-1.662930 \] \[ k_4 = -\frac{2(5+0.1k_3)} {1+(5+0.1k_3)} \] \[ = -\frac{2(4.833707)} {5.833707} \] \[ k_4=-1.659072 \] \[ S_1 = 5 + \frac{0.1}{6} \Big[ -1.666667 +2(-1.662921) +2(-1.662930) -1.659072 \Big] \] \[ S_1=4.833707 \]

Step 2 : \(t=0.1 \rightarrow 0.2\)

\[ S_1=4.833707 \] \[ k_1 = -\frac{2(4.833707)} {5.833707} = -1.659072 \] \[ k_2 = -\frac{2(4.750754)} {5.750754} = -1.652123 \] \[ k_3 = -\frac{2(4.751101)} {5.751101} = -1.652155 \] \[ k_4 = -\frac{2(4.668492)} {5.668492} = -1.647090 \] \[ S_2 = 4.833707 + \frac{0.1}{6} \Big[ -1.659072 +2(-1.652123) +2(-1.652155) -1.647090 \Big] \] \[ S_2=4.668493 \]

Step 3 : \(t=0.2 \rightarrow 0.3\)

\[ k_1=-1.647090 \] \[ k_2=-1.641874 \] \[ k_3=-1.641908 \] \[ k_4=-1.636524 \] \[ S_3 = 4.668493 + \frac{0.1}{6} \Big[ -1.647090 +2(-1.641874) +2(-1.641908) -1.636524 \Big] \] \[ S_3=4.504306 \]

Step 4 : \(t=0.3 \rightarrow 0.4\)

\[ k_1=-1.636524 \] \[ k_2=-1.631070 \] \[ k_3=-1.631105 \] \[ k_4=-1.625465 \] \[ S_4 = 4.504306 + \frac{0.1}{6} \Big[ -1.636524 +2(-1.631070) +2(-1.631105) -1.625465 \Big] \] \[ S_4=4.341217 \]

Step 5 : \(t=0.4 \rightarrow 0.5\)

\[ k_1=-1.625465 \] \[ k_2=-1.619800 \] \[ k_3=-1.619837 \] \[ k_4=-1.613949 \] \[ S_5 = 4.341217 + \frac{0.1}{6} \Big[ -1.625465 +2(-1.619800) +2(-1.619837) -1.613949 \Big] \] \[ S_5=4.179264 \]

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{ S(0.5) \approx 4.1793 \; mol/L } \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P3 RK4 Michaelis-Menten

Enzyme Kinetics — RK4 Method
%% P3 — RK4 Method: Michaelis-Menten Enzyme Kinetics
      
      clc;
      clear;
      close all;
      
      Vmax = 2;
      Km = 1;
      
      h = 0.1;
      t0 = 0;
      tf = 0.5;
      S0 = 5;
      
      t = t0:h:tf;
      N = length(t);
      
      S = zeros(1, N);
      S(1) = S0;
      
      f = @(t,S) -Vmax*S/(Km + S);
      
      k1 = zeros(1, N-1);
      k2 = zeros(1, N-1);
      k3 = zeros(1, N-1);
      k4 = zeros(1, N-1);
      
      for n = 1:N-1
      
          k1(n) = f(t(n), S(n));
      
          k2(n) = f(t(n) + h/2, S(n) + (h/2)*k1(n));
      
          k3(n) = f(t(n) + h/2, S(n) + (h/2)*k2(n));
      
          k4(n) = f(t(n) + h, S(n) + h*k3(n));
      
          S(n+1) = S(n) + (h/6)*(k1(n) + 2*k2(n) + 2*k3(n) + k4(n));
      
      end
      
      Results = table(t', S', ...
          'VariableNames', {'t', 'RK4_S'});
      
      disp(Results)
      
      fprintf('S(0.5) = %.6f mol/L\n', S(end))
P4 FDM 1D — Extended Fin Heat Transfer

An extended fin with convection losses:

\[ \frac{d^2T}{dx^2} - 4T = 0, \quad T(0) = 10, \quad T(1) = 0 \]

Use FDM with \(N=4\) interior nodes (\(h=0.1\)). Set up and solve the tridiagonal system.

Note: \( y_{i-1} - (2 + 4h^2)y_i + y_{i+1} = 0 \) gives \( y_{i-1} - 2.25y_i + y_{i+1} = 0 \)

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

The temperature distribution in an extended fin is governed by

\[ \frac{d^2T}{dx^2}-4T=0 \] with boundary conditions \[ T(0)=10 \] \[ T(0.5)=0 \]

Use the Finite Difference Method with

\[ h=0.1 \]

to obtain the nodal temperatures inside the domain.

Step 1: Generate Grid Points

\[ x_0=0 \] \[ x_1=0.1 \] \[ x_2=0.2 \] \[ x_3=0.3 \] \[ x_4=0.4 \] \[ x_5=0.5 \] Boundary values: \[ T_0=10 \] \[ T_5=0 \] Unknowns: \[ T_1,\;T_2,\;T_3,\;T_4 \]

Step 2: Finite Difference Approximation

Central difference approximation: \[ \frac{d^2T}{dx^2} \approx \frac{T_{i-1}-2T_i+T_{i+1}}{h^2} \] Substitute into the differential equation: \[ \frac{T_{i-1}-2T_i+T_{i+1}}{h^2} -4T_i=0 \] Since \[ h=0.1 \] then \[ h^2=0.01 \] Multiply the equation by \(0.01\): \[ T_{i-1}-2T_i+T_{i+1}-0.04T_i=0 \] \[ T_{i-1}-2.04T_i+T_{i+1}=0 \] This equation is applied at every interior node.

Step 3: Equation at Node 1

\[ T_0-2.04T_1+T_2=0 \] Substitute \(T_0=10\): \[ 10-2.04T_1+T_2=0 \] \[ -2.04T_1+T_2=-10 \]

Step 4: Equation at Node 2

\[ T_1-2.04T_2+T_3=0 \]

Step 5: Equation at Node 3

\[ T_2-2.04T_3+T_4=0 \]

Step 6: Equation at Node 4

\[ T_3-2.04T_4+T_5=0 \] Since \[ T_5=0 \] \[ T_3-2.04T_4=0 \]

Step 7: Matrix Form

\[ \begin{bmatrix} -2.04 & 1 & 0 & 0\\ 1 & -2.04 & 1 & 0\\ 0 & 1 & -2.04 & 1\\ 0 & 0 & 1 & -2.04 \end{bmatrix} \begin{bmatrix} T_1\\ T_2\\ T_3\\ T_4 \end{bmatrix} = \begin{bmatrix} -10\\ 0\\ 0\\ 0 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 8: Gaussian Elimination

Initial augmented matrix: \[ \left[ \begin{array}{cccc|c} -2.04&1&0&0&-10\\ 1&-2.04&1&0&0\\ 0&1&-2.04&1&0\\ 0&0&1&-2.04&0 \end{array} \right] \] Eliminate \(T_1\) from Row 2: \[ R_2 \leftarrow R_2+\frac{1}{2.04}R_1 \] \[ \left[ \begin{array}{cccc|c} -2.04&1&0&0&-10\\ 0&-1.549804&1&0&-4.901961\\ 0&1&-2.04&1&0\\ 0&0&1&-2.04&0 \end{array} \right] \] Eliminate \(T_2\) from Row 3: \[ R_3 \leftarrow R_3+\frac{1}{1.549804}R_2 \] \[ \left[ \begin{array}{cccc|c} -2.04&1&0&0&-10\\ 0&-1.549804&1&0&-4.901961\\ 0&0&-1.394434&1&-3.163928\\ 0&0&1&-2.04&0 \end{array} \right] \] Eliminate \(T_3\) from Row 4: \[ R_4 \leftarrow R_4+\frac{1}{1.394434}R_3 \] \[ \left[ \begin{array}{cccc|c} -2.04&1&0&0&-10\\ 0&-1.549804&1&0&-4.901961\\ 0&0&-1.394434&1&-3.163928\\ 0&0&0&-1.322871&-2.268636 \end{array} \right] \]

Step 9: Back Substitution

From Row 4: \[ -1.322871T_4=-2.268636 \] \[ T_4=1.7142 \]
From Row 3: \[ -1.394434T_3+T_4=-3.163928 \] \[ -1.394434T_3+1.7142=-3.163928 \] \[ T_3=3.4985 \]
From Row 2: \[ -1.549804T_2+T_3=-4.901961 \] \[ -1.549804T_2+3.4985=-4.901961 \] \[ T_2=5.4202 \]
From Row 1: \[ -2.04T_1+T_2=-10 \] \[ -2.04T_1+5.4202=-10 \] \[ T_1=7.5589 \]

Final Nodal Temperatures

\[ T_0=10 \] \[ T_1=7.5589 \] \[ T_2=5.4202 \] \[ T_3=3.4985 \] \[ T_4=1.7142 \] \[ T_5=0 \] Therefore, \[ \boxed{ T(x) \approx \{10,\;7.5589,\;5.4202,\;3.4985,\;1.7142,\;0\} } \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P4 FDM 1D with Gaussian Elimination

Extended Fin Heat Transfer — FDM + Gaussian Elimination
%% P4 — FDM 1D Extended Fin with Gaussian Elimination
      
      clc;
      clear;
      close all;
      
      % Problem:
      % d2T/dx2 - 4T = 0
      % T(0) = 10, T(0.5) = 0
      % h = 0.1 gives 4 interior nodes
      
      h = 0.1;
      T0 = 10;
      T5 = 0;
      
      N = 4;
      
      mainCoeff = -(2 + 4*h^2);
      
      A = zeros(N,N);
      b = zeros(N,1);
      
      for i = 1:N
          A(i,i) = mainCoeff;
      
          if i > 1
              A(i,i-1) = 1;
          else
              b(i) = b(i) - T0;
          end
      
          if i < N
              A(i,i+1) = 1;
          else
              b(i) = b(i) - T5;
          end
      end
      
      %% Gaussian Elimination with Partial Pivoting
      
      Aug = [A b];
      n = length(b);
      
      for k = 1:n-1
      
          [~, maxRow] = max(abs(Aug(k:n,k)));
          maxRow = maxRow + k - 1;
      
          if maxRow ~= k
              temp = Aug(k,:);
              Aug(k,:) = Aug(maxRow,:);
              Aug(maxRow,:) = temp;
          end
      
          for i = k+1:n
              multiplier = Aug(i,k)/Aug(k,k);
              Aug(i,:) = Aug(i,:) - multiplier*Aug(k,:);
          end
      
      end
      
      %% Back Substitution
      
      T_unknown = zeros(n,1);
      
      T_unknown(n) = Aug(n,end)/Aug(n,n);
      
      for i = n-1:-1:1
          T_unknown(i) = (Aug(i,end) - Aug(i,i+1:n)*T_unknown(i+1:n))/Aug(i,i);
      end
      
      T_full = [T0; T_unknown; T5];
      
      x = (0:h:0.5)';
      
      Results = table(x, T_full, ...
          'VariableNames', {'x', 'Temperature'});
      
      disp('Coefficient matrix A:')
      disp(A)
      
      disp('Right-hand side b:')
      disp(b)
      
      disp('Temperature Results:')
      disp(Results)
      
      plot(x, T_full, '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
      grid on;
      xlabel('x');
      ylabel('Temperature T');
      title('FDM 1D Extended Fin Temperature Distribution');
P5 RK4 — Logistic Bioreactor Growth

Biomass growth in a batch bioreactor follows the logistic model:

\[ \frac{dX}{dt}=0.8X\left(1-\frac{X}{10}\right) \]

Given \(X(0)=1.0\;g/L\), use RK4 with \(h=0.5\;h\) to estimate \(X(2.5)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

RK4 Formula

\[ k_1=f(t_n,X_n) \] \[ k_2=f\left(t_n+\frac h2,X_n+\frac h2k_1\right) \] \[ k_3=f\left(t_n+\frac h2,X_n+\frac h2k_2\right) \] \[ k_4=f(t_n+h,X_n+hk_3) \] \[ X_{n+1}=X_n+\frac h6(k_1+2k_2+2k_3+k_4) \]

Step 1: \(t=0\rightarrow0.5\)

\[ X_0=1.0000 \] \[ k_1=0.8(1)(1-1/10)=0.7200 \] \[ k_2=0.8326,\qquad k_3=0.8498,\qquad k_4=0.9775 \] \[ X_1=1+\frac{0.5}{6}[0.7200+2(0.8326)+2(0.8498)+0.9775] \] \[ X_1=1.4219 \]

Step 2: \(t=0.5\rightarrow1.0\)

\[ X_1=1.4219 \] \[ k_1=0.9757,\qquad k_2=1.1106,\qquad k_3=1.1285,\qquad k_4=1.2733 \] \[ X_2=1.4219+\frac{0.5}{6}[0.9757+2(1.1106)+2(1.1285)+1.2733] \] \[ X_2=1.9825 \]

Step 3: \(t=1.0\rightarrow1.5\)

\[ X_2=1.9825 \] \[ k_1=1.2716,\qquad k_2=1.4170,\qquad k_3=1.4326,\qquad k_4=1.5763 \] \[ X_3=1.9825+\frac{0.5}{6}[1.2716+2(1.4170)+2(1.4326)+1.5763] \] \[ X_3=2.6947 \]

Step 4: \(t=1.5\rightarrow2.0\)

\[ X_3=2.6947 \] \[ k_1=1.5749,\qquad k_2=1.7077,\qquad k_3=1.7177,\qquad k_4=1.8326 \] \[ X_4=2.6947+\frac{0.5}{6}[1.5749+2(1.7077)+2(1.7177)+1.8326] \] \[ X_4=3.5496 \]

Step 5: \(t=2.0\rightarrow2.5\)

\[ X_4=3.5496 \] \[ k_1=1.8317,\qquad k_2=1.9212,\qquad k_3=1.9247,\qquad k_4=1.9809 \] \[ X_5=3.5496+\frac{0.5}{6}[1.8317+2(1.9212)+2(1.9247)+1.9809] \] \[ \boxed{X(2.5)=4.5083\;g/L} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — RK4 Logistic Growth

Bioreactor Logistic Growth
%% P5 — RK4 Logistic Bioreactor Growth
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  r = 0.8;
  K = 10;
  
  h = 0.5;
  t0 = 0;
  tf = 2.5;
  X0 = 1;
  
  t = t0:h:tf;
  N = length(t);
  
  X = zeros(1,N);
  X(1) = X0;
  
  f = @(t,X) r*X*(1 - X/K);
  
  k1 = zeros(1,N-1);
  k2 = zeros(1,N-1);
  k3 = zeros(1,N-1);
  k4 = zeros(1,N-1);
  
  for n = 1:N-1
  
      k1(n) = f(t(n), X(n));
  
      k2(n) = f(t(n)+h/2, X(n)+(h/2)*k1(n));
  
      k3(n) = f(t(n)+h/2, X(n)+(h/2)*k2(n));
  
      k4(n) = f(t(n)+h, X(n)+h*k3(n));
  
      X(n+1) = X(n) + (h/6)*(k1(n)+2*k2(n)+2*k3(n)+k4(n));
  
  end
  
  Results = table(t', X', ...
      'VariableNames', {'Time_h', 'Biomass_X_g_L'});
  
  disp(Results)
  
  fprintf('X(2.5) = %.4f g/L\n', X(end))
  
  plot(t,X,'-o','LineWidth',2);
  grid on;
  xlabel('Time (h)');
  ylabel('Biomass X (g/L)');
  title('RK4 Logistic Bioreactor Growth');
P6 RK2 Heun — Nonlinear Decay with Periodic Feed

A tank concentration follows nonlinear consumption with a periodic feed effect:

\[ \frac{dC}{dt}=-0.6C^2+0.2\sin(t) \]

Given \(C(0)=2.0\), use Heun's RK2 method with \(h=0.2\) to estimate \(C(1.0)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Heun Method

\[ k_1=f(t_n,C_n) \] \[ C^*=C_n+hk_1 \] \[ k_2=f(t_n+h,C^*) \] \[ C_{n+1}=C_n+\frac h2(k_1+k_2) \]

Step 1: \(t=0\rightarrow0.2\)

\[ C_0=2.0000 \] \[ k_1=-0.6(2)^2+0.2\sin(0)=-2.4000 \] \[ C^*=2+0.2(-2.4000)=1.5200 \] \[ k_2=-0.6(1.5200)^2+0.2\sin(0.2)=-1.3465 \] \[ C_1=2+\frac{0.2}{2}(-2.4000-1.3465) \] \[ C_1=1.6253 \]

Step 2: \(t=0.2\rightarrow0.4\)

\[ C_1=1.6253 \] \[ k_1=-1.5453 \] \[ C^*=1.6253+0.2(-1.5453)=1.3163 \] \[ k_2=-0.9617 \] \[ C_2=1.6253+0.1(-1.5453-0.9617) \] \[ C_2=1.3746 \]

Step 3: \(t=0.4\rightarrow0.6\)

\[ C_2=1.3746 \] \[ k_1=-1.0559 \] \[ C^*=1.3746+0.2(-1.0559)=1.1635 \] \[ k_2=-0.6993 \] \[ C_3=1.3746+0.1(-1.0559-0.6993) \] \[ C_3=1.1991 \]

Step 4: \(t=0.6\rightarrow0.8\)

\[ C_3=1.1991 \] \[ k_1=-0.7498 \] \[ C^*=1.1991+0.2(-0.7498)=1.0492 \] \[ k_2=-0.5170 \] \[ C_4=1.1991+0.1(-0.7498-0.5170) \] \[ C_4=1.0725 \]

Step 5: \(t=0.8\rightarrow1.0\)

\[ C_4=1.0725 \] \[ k_1=-0.5466 \] \[ C^*=1.0725+0.2(-0.5466)=0.9631 \] \[ k_2=-0.3883 \] \[ C_5=1.0725+0.1(-0.5466-0.3883) \] \[ \boxed{C(1.0)=0.9790} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — Heun Nonlinear Decay with Periodic Feed

RK2 Heun Method
%% P6 — RK2 Heun Method: Nonlinear Decay with Periodic Feed
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  h = 0.2;
  t0 = 0;
  tf = 1.0;
  C0 = 2.0;
  
  t = t0:h:tf;
  N = length(t);
  
  C = zeros(1,N);
  C(1) = C0;
  
  f = @(t,C) -0.6*C^2 + 0.2*sin(t);
  
  k1 = zeros(1,N-1);
  k2 = zeros(1,N-1);
  Cpred = zeros(1,N-1);
  
  for n = 1:N-1
  
      k1(n) = f(t(n), C(n));
  
      Cpred(n) = C(n) + h*k1(n);
  
      k2(n) = f(t(n)+h, Cpred(n));
  
      C(n+1) = C(n) + (h/2)*(k1(n)+k2(n));
  
  end
  
  Results = table(t', C', ...
      'VariableNames', {'Time', 'Concentration_C'});
  
  disp(Results)
  
  fprintf('C(1.0) = %.4f\n', C(end))
  
  plot(t,C,'-o','LineWidth',2);
  grid on;
  xlabel('Time');
  ylabel('Concentration C');
  title('Heun Method for Nonlinear Decay with Periodic Feed');
P7 Shooting Method — Complex BVP with RK4 + Secant

Solve the boundary value problem:

\[ y'' - y' - 2y = -x \] \[ y(0)=1,\qquad y(1)=2 \]

Use the shooting method with RK4, \(h=0.2\), and two initial guesses: \(s_1=0\), \(s_2=4\), where \(s=y'(0)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1 — Convert to First-Order System

\[ u_1=y,\qquad u_2=y' \] \[ u_1'=u_2 \] From: \[ y''-y'-2y=-x \] \[ y''=y'+2y-x \] Therefore: \[ u_2'=u_2+2u_1-x \] \[ \mathbf{u}'= \begin{bmatrix} u_2\\ u_2+2u_1-x \end{bmatrix} \]

Shoot 1: \(s_1=0\)

\[ u_1(0)=1,\qquad u_2(0)=0 \]
Step 1: \(x=0.0\to0.2\)
\(\mathbf{k}_1=[0.0000,\;2.0000]\)
\(\mathbf{k}_2=[0.2000,\;2.1000]\)
\(\mathbf{k}_3=[0.2100,\;2.1500]\)
\(\mathbf{k}_4=[0.4300,\;2.3140]\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[1.0417,\;0.4271] \]
Step 2: \(x=0.2\to0.4\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[1.1766,\;0.9423] \]
Step 3: \(x=0.4\to0.6\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[1.4287,\;1.6109] \]
Step 4: \(x=0.6\to0.8\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[1.8373,\;2.5266] \]
Step 5: \(x=0.8\to1.0\)
\[ [u_1(1),u_2(1)]=[2.4646,\;3.8255] \]
\[ F(0)=u_1(1)-2=2.4646-2=+0.4646 \]

Shoot 2: \(s_2=4\)

\[ u_1(0)=1,\qquad u_2(0)=4 \]
Step 1: \(x=0.0\to0.2\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[1.9390,\;5.4967] \]
Step 2: \(x=0.2\to0.4\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[3.2499,\;7.7701] \]
Step 3: \(x=0.4\to0.6\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[5.1229,\;11.1947] \]
Step 4: \(x=0.6\to0.8\)
\[ [u_1,u_2]=[7.8406,\;16.3305] \]
Step 5: \(x=0.8\to1.0\)
\[ [u_1(1),u_2(1)]=[11.8231,\;24.0141] \]
\[ F(4)=11.8231-2=+9.8231 \]

Secant Update

\[ s_{new} = s_2 - F(s_2) \frac{s_2-s_1}{F(s_2)-F(s_1)} \] \[ s_{new} = 4 - 9.8231 \frac{4-0}{9.8231-0.4646} \] \[ s_{new} = -0.1986 \]

Final Shoot with \(s=-0.1986\)

\[ y'(0)\approx -0.1986 \] \[ u_1(1)\approx 2.0000 \] \[ \boxed{y'(0)\approx -0.1986} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — Shooting Method with RK4 and Secant

Complex BVP Shooting Method
%% P5 — Shooting Method with RK4 and Secant Method
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  % BVP:
  % y'' - y' - 2y = -x
  % y(0) = 1, y(1) = 2
  
  a = 0;
  b = 1;
  alpha = 1;
  beta = 2;
  h = 0.2;
  
  x = a:h:b;
  N = length(x);
  
  % System:
  % u1 = y
  % u2 = y'
  % u1' = u2
  % u2' = u2 + 2u1 - x
  
  f = @(x,U) [U(2); U(2) + 2*U(1) - x];
  
  % Initial guesses for y'(0)
  s1 = 0;
  s2 = 4;
  
  [U1,F1] = shoot_rk4(f,x,h,alpha,s1,beta);
  [U2,F2] = shoot_rk4(f,x,h,alpha,s2,beta);
  
  % Secant method
  sNew = s2 - F2*(s2-s1)/(F2-F1);
  
  [UFinal,FFinal] = shoot_rk4(f,x,h,alpha,sNew,beta);
  
  fprintf('Guess s1 = %.4f, y(1) = %.4f, F = %.4f\n', s1, U1(1,end), F1)
  fprintf('Guess s2 = %.4f, y(1) = %.4f, F = %.4f\n', s2, U2(1,end), F2)
  fprintf('Secant slope = %.6f\n', sNew)
  fprintf('Final y(1) = %.6f\n', UFinal(1,end))
  fprintf('Final residual = %.6e\n', FFinal)
  
  Results = table(x', UFinal(1,:)', UFinal(2,:)', ...
      'VariableNames', {'x', 'y', 'y_prime'});
  
  disp(Results)
  
  plot(x,UFinal(1,:),'-o','LineWidth',2);
  grid on;
  xlabel('x');
  ylabel('y(x)');
  title('Shooting Method Solution');
  
  function [U,residual] = shoot_rk4(f,x,h,alpha,s,beta)
  
      N = length(x);
      U = zeros(2,N);
  
      U(:,1) = [alpha; s];
  
      for n = 1:N-1
  
          xn = x(n);
          Un = U(:,n);
  
          k1 = f(xn, Un);
          k2 = f(xn+h/2, Un+(h/2)*k1);
          k3 = f(xn+h/2, Un+(h/2)*k2);
          k4 = f(xn+h, Un+h*k3);
  
          U(:,n+1) = Un + (h/6)*(k1+2*k2+2*k3+k4);
  
      end
  
      residual = U(1,end) - beta;
  
  end
P8 2D FDM — Heat Transfer with Source and Mixed Boundaries

Solve the 2D steady heat-transfer problem:

\[ \nabla^2T=-160 \]

on a square plate \([0,1]\times[0,1]\), using \(h=0.25\), giving \(3\times3=9\) interior unknowns.

Boundary conditions: top \(=120^\circ C\), bottom \(=20^\circ C\), left \(=80^\circ C\), right \(=40^\circ C\).

Graphical Problem Layout

▶ Detailed Answer

Gaussian Elimination Hand Solution

The 2D FDM equations are:

\[ \begin{aligned} -4T_1+T_2+T_4&=-110\\ T_1-4T_2+T_3+T_5&=-30\\ T_2-4T_3+T_6&=-70\\ T_1-4T_4+T_5+T_7&=-90\\ T_2+T_4-4T_5+T_6+T_8&=-10\\ T_3+T_5-4T_6+T_9&=-50\\ T_4-4T_7+T_8&=-210\\ T_5+T_7-4T_8+T_9&=-130\\ T_6+T_8-4T_9&=-170 \end{aligned} \]

Augmented Matrix

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccccccccc|c} -4&1&0&1&0&0&0&0&0&-110\\ 1&-4&1&0&1&0&0&0&0&-30\\ 0&1&-4&0&0&1&0&0&0&-70\\ 1&0&0&-4&1&0&1&0&0&-90\\ 0&1&0&1&-4&1&0&1&0&-10\\ 0&0&1&0&1&-4&0&0&1&-50\\ 0&0&0&1&0&0&-4&1&0&-210\\ 0&0&0&0&1&0&1&-4&1&-130\\ 0&0&0&0&0&1&0&1&-4&-170 \end{array} \right] \]

Forward Elimination

1Eliminate below Column 1

Pivot in Row 1 is \(-4\).

\[ R_2 \leftarrow R_2+\frac{1}{4}R_1 \] \[ R_4 \leftarrow R_4+\frac{1}{4}R_1 \]

This removes the \(T_1\) terms from Rows 2 and 4.

\[ R_2=[0,\;-3.75,\;1,\;0.25,\;1,\;0,\;0,\;0,\;0\;|\;-57.5] \] \[ R_4=[0,\;0.25,\;0,\;-3.75,\;1,\;0,\;1,\;0,\;0\;|\;-117.5] \]
2Eliminate below Column 2

Pivot in Row 2 is \(-3.75\).

\[ R_3\leftarrow R_3+\frac{1}{3.75}R_2 \] \[ R_4\leftarrow R_4+\frac{0.25}{3.75}R_2 \] \[ R_5\leftarrow R_5+\frac{1}{3.75}R_2 \]

Important resulting rows:

\[ R_3=[0,\;0,\;-3.7333,\;0.0667,\;0.2667,\;1,\;0,\;0,\;0\;|\;-85.3333] \] \[ R_5=[0,\;0,\;0.2667,\;1.0667,\;-3.7333,\;1,\;0,\;1,\;0\;|\;-25.3333] \]
3Continue Forward Elimination to Upper Triangular Form

After eliminating all entries below the diagonal, the upper triangular system is:

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccccccccc|c} -4&1&0&1&0&0&0&0&0&-110\\ 0&-3.7500&1&0.2500&1&0&0&0&0&-57.5000\\ 0&0&-3.7333&0.0667&0.2667&1&0&0&0&-85.3333\\ 0&0&0&-3.7321&1.0714&0.0179&1&0&0&-122.8571\\ 0&0&0&0&-3.4067&1.0766&0.2871&1&0&-66.6986\\ 0&0&0&0&0&-3.3919&0.0955&0.3160&1&-94.5225\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&-3.7052&1.0932&0.0282&-251.2008\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&0&-3.3545&1.1015&-232.4989\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&0&0&-3.3433&-276.1194 \end{array} \right] \]

Back Substitution

4Solve from \(T_9\) upward to \(T_1\)

Row 9:

\[ -3.3433T_9=-276.1194 \] \[ T_9=82.5893 \]

Row 8:

\[ -3.3545T_8+1.1015T_9=-232.4989 \] \[ -3.3545T_8+1.1015(82.5893)=-232.4989 \] \[ T_8=96.4286 \]

Row 7:

\[ -3.7052T_7+1.0932T_8+0.0282T_9=-251.2008 \] \[ T_7=96.8750 \]

Row 6:

\[ -3.3919T_6+0.0955T_7+0.3160T_8+T_9=-94.5225 \] \[ T_6=63.9286 \]

Row 5:

\[ -3.4067T_5+1.0766T_6+0.2871T_7+T_8=-66.6986 \] \[ T_5=76.2500 \]

Row 4:

\[ -3.7321T_4+1.0714T_5+0.0179T_6+T_7=-122.8571 \] \[ T_4=81.0714 \]

Row 3:

\[ -3.7333T_3+0.0667T_4+0.2667T_5+T_6=-85.3333 \] \[ T_3=46.8750 \]

Row 2:

\[ -3.7500T_2+T_3+0.2500T_4+T_5=-57.5000 \] \[ T_2=53.5714 \]

Row 1:

\[ -4T_1+T_2+T_4=-110 \] \[ -4T_1+53.5714+81.0714=-110 \] \[ T_1=61.1607 \]

Final Temperature Field

\[ \boxed{ \begin{aligned} T_1&=61.1607,& T_2&=53.5714,& T_3&=46.8750\\ T_4&=81.0714,& T_5&=76.2500,& T_6&=63.9286\\ T_7&=96.8750,& T_8&=96.4286,& T_9&=82.5893 \end{aligned} } \]

Temperature Grid

\[ \begin{matrix} T_7 & T_8 & T_9\\ T_4 & T_5 & T_6\\ T_1 & T_2 & T_3 \end{matrix} = \begin{matrix} 96.8750 & 96.4286 & 82.5893\\ 81.0714 & 76.2500 & 63.9286\\ 61.1607 & 53.5714 & 46.8750 \end{matrix} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — 2D FDM with Gaussian Elimination

2D Poisson Heat Transfer
%% P6 — 2D FDM Heat Transfer with Gaussian Elimination
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  % PDE:
  % Laplacian(T) = -160
  
  h = 0.25;
  source = -160*h^2;   % = -10
  
  Nx = 3;
  Ny = 3;
  N = Nx*Ny;
  
  T_top = 120;
  T_bottom = 20;
  T_left = 80;
  T_right = 40;
  
  A = zeros(N,N);
  b = source*ones(N,1);
  
  idx = @(i,j) (j-1)*Nx + i;
  
  %% Assemble A and b
  
  for j = 1:Ny
      for i = 1:Nx
  
          k = idx(i,j);
  
          A(k,k) = -4;
  
          if i > 1
              A(k,idx(i-1,j)) = 1;
          else
              b(k) = b(k) - T_left;
          end
  
          if i < Nx
              A(k,idx(i+1,j)) = 1;
          else
              b(k) = b(k) - T_right;
          end
  
          if j > 1
              A(k,idx(i,j-1)) = 1;
          else
              b(k) = b(k) - T_bottom;
          end
  
          if j < Ny
              A(k,idx(i,j+1)) = 1;
          else
              b(k) = b(k) - T_top;
          end
  
      end
  end
  
  %% Gaussian Elimination with Partial Pivoting
  
  Aug = [A b];
  n = length(b);
  
  for k = 1:n-1
  
      [~, maxRow] = max(abs(Aug(k:n,k)));
      maxRow = maxRow + k - 1;
  
      if maxRow ~= k
          temp = Aug(k,:);
          Aug(k,:) = Aug(maxRow,:);
          Aug(maxRow,:) = temp;
      end
  
      for i = k+1:n
          multiplier = Aug(i,k)/Aug(k,k);
          Aug(i,:) = Aug(i,:) - multiplier*Aug(k,:);
      end
  
  end
  
  %% Back Substitution
  
  T = zeros(n,1);
  
  T(n) = Aug(n,end)/Aug(n,n);
  
  for i = n-1:-1:1
      T(i) = (Aug(i,end) - Aug(i,i+1:n)*T(i+1:n))/Aug(i,i);
  end
  
  T_grid = reshape(T,Nx,Ny)';
  
  disp('Coefficient Matrix A:')
  disp(A)
  
  disp('Right-hand side b:')
  disp(b)
  
  disp('Temperature vector:')
  disp(T)
  
  disp('Temperature grid:')
  disp(T_grid)
  
  % Residual check
  residual = A*T - b;
  fprintf('Residual norm = %.4e\n', norm(residual))
  
  % Plot heatmap
  figure;
  imagesc(T_grid);
  set(gca,'YDir','normal');
  colorbar;
  axis equal tight;
  title('Interior Temperature Field');
  xlabel('i index');
  ylabel('j index');
P9 Trial-and-Error — Nonlinear CSTR Design

A liquid-phase reaction \(A \rightarrow B\) occurs in a CSTR. The reaction rate is nonlinear:

\[ -r_A = kC_A^2 \]

Given:

\[ F_{A0}=10\;mol/min,\qquad C_{A0}=2\;mol/L \] \[ k=0.15\;L/(mol\cdot min),\qquad V=20\;L \]

Find the conversion \(X\) using the trial-and-error fixed point method.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1 — CSTR Design Equation

\[ V=\frac{F_{A0}X}{-r_A} \] Since: \[ C_A=C_{A0}(1-X) \] \[ C_A=2(1-X) \] The rate law becomes: \[ -r_A=kC_A^2 \] \[ -r_A=0.15[2(1-X)]^2 \] \[ -r_A=0.6(1-X)^2 \] Substitute into the CSTR design equation: \[ 20=\frac{10X}{0.6(1-X)^2} \] Multiply both sides: \[ 20[0.6(1-X)^2]=10X \] \[ 12(1-X)^2=10X \] Expand: \[ 12(1-2X+X^2)=10X \] \[ 12-24X+12X^2=10X \] \[ 12X^2-34X+12=0 \]

Step 2 — Rearrange for Trial-and-Error

For fixed point trial-and-error, rearrange the equation into the form:

\[ X_{new}=g(X_{old}) \] Starting from: \[ 12X^2-34X+12=0 \] Move the middle term: \[ 34X=12X^2+12 \] Divide by 34: \[ \boxed{ X_{new}=\frac{12X_{old}^2+12}{34} } \]
Important: In trial-and-error fixed point iteration, the answer from each trial becomes the guess for the next trial.

Trial 1

\[ X_0=0.3000 \] \[ X_1=\frac{12(0.3000)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_1=\frac{12(0.0900)+12}{34} \] \[ X_1=\frac{1.0800+12}{34} \] \[ X_1=0.3847 \]

The answer \(0.3847\) becomes the next guess.

Trial 2

\[ X_1=0.3847 \] \[ X_2=\frac{12(0.3847)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_2=\frac{12(0.14799)+12}{34} \] \[ X_2=\frac{1.7759+12}{34} \] \[ X_2=0.4052 \]

Trial 3

\[ X_2=0.4052 \] \[ X_3=\frac{12(0.4052)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_3=\frac{12(0.1642)+12}{34} \] \[ X_3=\frac{1.9704+12}{34} \] \[ X_3=0.4109 \]

Trial 4

\[ X_3=0.4109 \] \[ X_4=\frac{12(0.4109)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_4=\frac{12(0.1688)+12}{34} \] \[ X_4=\frac{2.0256+12}{34} \] \[ X_4=0.4125 \]

Trial 5

\[ X_4=0.4125 \] \[ X_5=\frac{12(0.4125)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_5=\frac{12(0.1702)+12}{34} \] \[ X_5=\frac{2.0424+12}{34} \] \[ X_5=0.4130 \]

Trial 6

\[ X_5=0.4130 \] \[ X_6=\frac{12(0.4130)^2+12}{34} \] \[ X_6=\frac{12(0.1706)+12}{34} \] \[ X_6=\frac{2.0472+12}{34} \] \[ X_6=0.4132 \]

Convergence Table

Trial Old Guess \(X_{old}\) New Answer \(X_{new}\) Error \(|X_{new}-X_{old}|\)
10.30000.38470.0847
20.38470.40520.0205
30.40520.41090.0057
40.41090.41250.0016
50.41250.41300.0005
60.41300.41320.0002

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{X\approx0.4132} \] \[ \boxed{X\approx41.32\%} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — Trial-and-Error Fixed Point Iteration

Nonlinear CSTR Conversion
%% P9 - Trial-and-Error Fixed Point Iteration
  % Reaction:
  % A -> B
  %
  % Rate law:
  % -rA = k*CA^2
  %
  % CSTR design equation:
  % V = FA0*X/(-rA)
  %
  % Rearranged fixed point form:
  % X_new = (12*X_old^2 + 12)/34
  %
  % The answer from each trial becomes the next guess.
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  %% Step 1: Given data
  
  FA0 = 10;       % mol/min
  CA0 = 2;        % mol/L
  k = 0.15;       % L/(mol min)
  V = 20;         % L
  
  %% Step 2: Initial guess
  
  Xold = 0.30;
  
  %% Step 3: Iteration settings
  
  tol = 1e-6;
  maxIter = 50;
  
  %% Step 4: Storage arrays
  
  Trial = [];
  OldGuess = [];
  NewAnswer = [];
  Error = [];
  
  %% Step 5: Trial-and-error iteration
  
  for n = 1:maxIter
  
      % Fixed point formula
      Xnew = (12*Xold^2 + 12) / 34;
  
      % Difference between new answer and old guess
      err = abs(Xnew - Xold);
  
      % Store results
      Trial(end+1) = n;
      OldGuess(end+1) = Xold;
      NewAnswer(end+1) = Xnew;
      Error(end+1) = err;
  
      % Print each trial
      fprintf('Trial %d\n', n);
      fprintf('Old guess  = %.6f\n', Xold);
      fprintf('New answer = %.6f\n', Xnew);
      fprintf('Error      = %.6e\n\n', err);
  
      % Check convergence
      if err < tol
          break
      end
  
      % Important trial-and-error step:
      % the answer becomes the next guess
      Xold = Xnew;
  
  end
  
  %% Step 6: Results table
  
  Results = table(Trial', OldGuess', NewAnswer', Error', ...
      'VariableNames', ...
      {'Trial', 'Old_Guess', 'New_Answer', 'Error'});
  
  disp('Trial-and-Error Results:')
  disp(Results)
  
  %% Step 7: Final conversion
  
  fprintf('Final conversion X = %.6f\n', Xnew);
  fprintf('Final conversion = %.2f percent\n', Xnew*100);
  
  %% Step 8: Check original CSTR equation
  
  CA = CA0*(1 - Xnew);
  rate = k*CA^2;
  Vcheck = FA0*Xnew/rate;
  
  fprintf('Check volume from final X = %.6f L\n', Vcheck);
  
  %% Step 9: Plot convergence
  
  figure;
  plot(Trial, NewAnswer, '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
  grid on;
  
  xlabel('Trial Number');
  ylabel('Conversion X');
  title('Trial-and-Error Convergence');
  
  %% Step 10: Plot error
  
  figure;
  semilogy(Trial, Error, '-s', 'LineWidth', 2);
  grid on;
  
  xlabel('Trial Number');
  ylabel('Absolute Error');
  title('Error Reduction in Trial-and-Error Method');
P10 Trial-and-Error — Complex Multi-Step CSTR Reaction Network

A liquid-phase reaction network occurs in a continuous stirred tank reactor:

\[ A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C \]

with an unwanted side reaction:

\[ A \rightarrow D \]

The rates are:

\[ r_1=\frac{k_1C_A}{K_m+C_A} \] \[ r_2=k_2C_B^2 \] \[ r_3=k_3C_A^2 \]

Given:

\[ C_{A0}=5.0\;mol/L,\qquad \tau=0.5\;min \] \[ k_1=2.0,\qquad K_m=1.0,\qquad k_2=0.15,\qquad k_3=0.05 \]

Use the trial-and-error fixed point method to find the steady-state concentrations \(C_A\) and \(C_B\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1 — Steady-State CSTR Balances

For species \(A\):

\[ C_A=C_{A0}-\tau(r_1+r_3) \]

For species \(B\):

\[ C_B=\tau(r_1-r_2) \]

Substitute the rates:

\[ C_A=5-0.5\left(\frac{2C_A}{1+C_A}+0.05C_A^2\right) \] \[ C_B=0.5\left(\frac{2C_A}{1+C_A}-0.15C_B^2\right) \]

Step 2 — Fixed Point Form

\[ C_{A,new}=5-0.5\left(\frac{2C_{A,old}}{1+C_{A,old}}+0.05C_{A,old}^2\right) \] \[ C_{B,new}=0.5\left(\frac{2C_{A,old}}{1+C_{A,old}}-0.15C_{B,old}^2\right) \]
Trial-and-error rule: the answer from each trial becomes the guess for the next trial.

Initial Guess

\[ C_A^{(0)}=4.0000,\qquad C_B^{(0)}=0.5000 \]

Trial 1

\[ r_1=\frac{2(4.0000)}{1+4.0000}=1.6000 \] \[ r_2=0.15(0.5000)^2=0.0375 \] \[ r_3=0.05(4.0000)^2=0.8000 \] \[ C_A^{(1)}=5-0.5(1.6000+0.8000)=3.8000 \] \[ C_B^{(1)}=0.5(1.6000-0.0375)=0.7813 \]

Trial 2

\[ C_A^{(1)}=3.8000,\qquad C_B^{(1)}=0.7813 \] \[ r_1=\frac{2(3.8000)}{1+3.8000}=1.5833 \] \[ r_2=0.15(0.7813)^2=0.0916 \] \[ r_3=0.05(3.8000)^2=0.7220 \] \[ C_A^{(2)}=5-0.5(1.5833+0.7220)=3.8473 \] \[ C_B^{(2)}=0.5(1.5833-0.0916)=0.7459 \]

Trial 3

\[ C_A^{(2)}=3.8473,\qquad C_B^{(2)}=0.7459 \] \[ r_1=\frac{2(3.8473)}{1+3.8473}=1.5874 \] \[ r_2=0.15(0.7459)^2=0.0835 \] \[ r_3=0.05(3.8473)^2=0.7401 \] \[ C_A^{(3)}=5-0.5(1.5874+0.7401)=3.8362 \] \[ C_B^{(3)}=0.5(1.5874-0.0835)=0.7520 \]

Trial 4

\[ C_A^{(3)}=3.8362,\qquad C_B^{(3)}=0.7520 \] \[ r_1=1.5865 \] \[ r_2=0.0848 \] \[ r_3=0.7358 \] \[ C_A^{(4)}=5-0.5(1.5865+0.7358)=3.8389 \] \[ C_B^{(4)}=0.5(1.5865-0.0848)=0.7508 \]

Trial 5

\[ C_A^{(4)}=3.8389,\qquad C_B^{(4)}=0.7508 \] \[ r_1=1.5867 \] \[ r_2=0.0846 \] \[ r_3=0.7368 \] \[ C_A^{(5)}=5-0.5(1.5867+0.7368)=3.8382 \] \[ C_B^{(5)}=0.5(1.5867-0.0846)=0.7511 \]

Convergence Table

Trial \(C_A^{old}\) \(C_B^{old}\) \(C_A^{new}\) \(C_B^{new}\)
14.00000.50003.80000.7813
23.80000.78133.84730.7459
33.84730.74593.83620.7520
43.83620.75203.83890.7508
53.83890.75083.83820.7511

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{C_A\approx3.838\;mol/L} \] \[ \boxed{C_B\approx0.751\;mol/L} \]
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — Trial-and-Error Multi-Step Reactor

Fixed Point Iteration for Multi-Step CSTR
%% P9 - Trial-and-Error for Multi-Step CSTR Reaction Network
  % Reaction network:
  %
  %     A -> B -> C
  %     A -> D   side reaction
  %
  % Rates:
  %     r1 = k1*CA/(Km + CA)
  %     r2 = k2*CB^2
  %     r3 = k3*CA^2
  %
  % CSTR fixed point equations:
  %     CA_new = CA0 - tau*(r1 + r3)
  %     CB_new = tau*(r1 - r2)
  %
  % The answer from each trial becomes the guess for the next trial.
  
  clc;
  clear;
  close all;
  
  %% Given data
  
  CA0 = 5.0;
  tau = 0.5;
  
  k1 = 2.0;
  Km = 1.0;
  k2 = 0.15;
  k3 = 0.05;
  
  %% Initial guesses
  
  CA_old = 4.0;
  CB_old = 0.5;
  
  %% Iteration settings
  
  tol = 1e-6;
  maxIter = 50;
  
  %% Storage arrays
  
  Trial = [];
  CA_guess = [];
  CB_guess = [];
  CA_new_store = [];
  CB_new_store = [];
  Error = [];
  
  %% Trial-and-error fixed point iteration
  
  for n = 1:maxIter
  
      % Calculate reaction rates using old guesses
      r1 = k1*CA_old/(Km + CA_old);
      r2 = k2*CB_old^2;
      r3 = k3*CA_old^2;
  
      % Fixed point equations
      CA_new = CA0 - tau*(r1 + r3);
      CB_new = tau*(r1 - r2);
  
      % Error between old guess and new answer
      err = max(abs([CA_new - CA_old, CB_new - CB_old]));
  
      % Store values
      Trial(end+1) = n;
      CA_guess(end+1) = CA_old;
      CB_guess(end+1) = CB_old;
      CA_new_store(end+1) = CA_new;
      CB_new_store(end+1) = CB_new;
      Error(end+1) = err;
  
      % Print trial
      fprintf('Trial %d\n', n);
      fprintf('Old CA = %.6f, Old CB = %.6f\n', CA_old, CB_old);
      fprintf('New CA = %.6f, New CB = %.6f\n', CA_new, CB_new);
      fprintf('Error  = %.6e\n\n', err);
  
      % Stop if converged
      if err < tol
          break
      end
  
      % IMPORTANT:
      % The answer becomes the next guess
      CA_old = CA_new;
      CB_old = CB_new;
  
  end
  
  %% Results table
  
  Results = table(Trial', CA_guess', CB_guess', CA_new_store', CB_new_store', Error', ...
      'VariableNames', ...
      {'Trial', ...
       'CA_old', ...
       'CB_old', ...
       'CA_new', ...
       'CB_new', ...
       'Error'});
  
  disp('Trial-and-Error Results:')
  disp(Results)
  
  %% Final answer
  
  fprintf('Final CA = %.6f mol/L\n', CA_new);
  fprintf('Final CB = %.6f mol/L\n', CB_new);
  
  %% Final reaction rates
  
  r1_final = k1*CA_new/(Km + CA_new);
  r2_final = k2*CB_new^2;
  r3_final = k3*CA_new^2;
  
  fprintf('Final r1 = %.6f\n', r1_final);
  fprintf('Final r2 = %.6f\n', r2_final);
  fprintf('Final r3 = %.6f\n', r3_final);
  
  %% Plot convergence
  
  figure;
  plot(Trial, CA_new_store, '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
  hold on;
  plot(Trial, CB_new_store, '-s', 'LineWidth', 2);
  grid on;
  
  xlabel('Trial Number');
  ylabel('Concentration (mol/L)');
  title('Trial-and-Error Convergence for Multi-Step CSTR');
  legend('C_A', 'C_B', 'Location', 'best');
  
  %% Plot error reduction
  
  figure;
  semilogy(Trial, Error, '-d', 'LineWidth', 2);
  grid on;
  
  xlabel('Trial Number');
  ylabel('Maximum Absolute Error');
  title('Error Reduction in Fixed Point Iteration');
P11 Coupled RK4 System — Non-Isothermal CSTR Startup

An exothermic first-order reaction \(A \rightarrow B\) takes place in a continuously stirred tank reactor. The concentration and temperature change together during startup:

\[ \frac{dC_A}{dt} = \frac{C_{Af}-C_A}{\tau} - k(T)C_A \] \[ \frac{dT}{dt} = \frac{T_f-T}{\tau} + 18k(T)C_A - 0.4(T-T_c) \] \[ k(T)=0.6e^{0.03(T-300)} \]

Given \(C_{Af}=2.0\;mol/L\), \(\tau=3\;min\), \(T_f=300\;K\), \(T_c=290\;K\), \(C_A(0)=1.2\;mol/L\), and \(T(0)=295\;K\), use RK4 for a coupled system with \(h=0.25\;min\) to estimate \(C_A(1.0)\) and \(T(1.0)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

\[ C_{Af}=2.0,\qquad \tau=3,\qquad T_f=300,\qquad T_c=290 \] \[ C_A(0)=1.2,\qquad T(0)=295,\qquad h=0.25 \]

Define the state vector:

\[ \mathbf{U} = \begin{bmatrix} C_A\\ T \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}' = \mathbf{f}(t,\mathbf{U}) = \begin{bmatrix} \dfrac{2-C_A}{3}-k(T)C_A\\[8pt] \dfrac{300-T}{3}+18k(T)C_A-0.4(T-290) \end{bmatrix} \] \[ k(T)=0.6e^{0.03(T-300)} \]

Vector RK4 Formula

\[ \mathbf{k}_1=\mathbf{f}(t_n,\mathbf{U}_n) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+\frac h2,\mathbf{U}_n+\frac h2\mathbf{k}_1\right) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+\frac h2,\mathbf{U}_n+\frac h2\mathbf{k}_2\right) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+h,\mathbf{U}_n+h\mathbf{k}_3\right) \] \[ \mathbf{U}_{n+1} = \mathbf{U}_n + \frac h6 \left( \mathbf{k}_1+2\mathbf{k}_2+2\mathbf{k}_3+\mathbf{k}_4 \right) \]

Step 1: \(t=0 \rightarrow 0.25\)

\[ \mathbf{U}_0= \begin{bmatrix} 1.2000\\ 295.0000 \end{bmatrix} \]

First compute the temperature-dependent rate constant:

\[ k(295)=0.6e^{0.03(295-300)} = 0.5164 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1 = \begin{bmatrix} -0.353043\\ 10.821442 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_0+\frac{h}{2}\mathbf{k}_1 = \begin{bmatrix} 1.155870\\ 296.352680 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2 = \begin{bmatrix} -0.340264\\ 9.864242 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_0+\frac{h}{2}\mathbf{k}_2 = \begin{bmatrix} 1.157467\\ 296.233030 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3 = \begin{bmatrix} -0.339425\\ 9.927301 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_0+h\mathbf{k}_3 = \begin{bmatrix} 1.115144\\ 297.481825 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4 = \begin{bmatrix} -0.325450\\ 9.013897 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_1 = \mathbf{U}_0 + \frac{0.25}{6} \left[ \mathbf{k}_1+2\mathbf{k}_2+2\mathbf{k}_3+\mathbf{k}_4 \right] \] \[ \mathbf{U}_1 = \begin{bmatrix} 1.115089\\ 297.475768 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 2: \(t=0.25 \rightarrow 0.50\)

\[ \mathbf{U}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 1.115089\\ 297.475768 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -0.325288\\ 9.015760 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -0.309668\\ 8.152124 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -0.309440\\ 8.215466 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.293156\\ 7.395366 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_2 = \begin{bmatrix} 1.037728\\ 299.523530 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 3: \(t=0.50 \rightarrow 0.75\)

\[ \mathbf{U}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 1.037728\\ 299.523530 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -0.293043\\ 7.397810 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -0.275823\\ 6.629508 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -0.276094\\ 6.691902 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.258699\\ 5.966925 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_3 = \begin{bmatrix} 0.968745\\ 301.190512 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 4: \(t=0.75 \rightarrow 1.00\)

\[ \mathbf{U}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 0.968745\\ 301.190512 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -0.258630\\ 5.969832 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -0.240934\\ 5.298034 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -0.241576\\ 5.357903 \end{bmatrix}, \qquad \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.224104\\ 4.728447 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{U}_4 = \begin{bmatrix} 0.908422\\ 302.524268 \end{bmatrix} \]

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{ C_A(1.0)=0.9084\;mol/L } \] \[ \boxed{ T(1.0)=302.5243\;K } \]

The concentration decreases because reactant \(A\) is consumed, while the reactor temperature rises because the exothermic heat-release term initially dominates the cooling term.

▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P11 Coupled RK4 Non-Isothermal CSTR

Non-Isothermal CSTR Startup — Coupled RK4
%% P11 — Coupled RK4 System: Non-Isothermal CSTR Startup

clc;
clear;
close all;

% Problem data
CAf = 2.0;      % mol/L
tau = 3.0;      % min
Tf  = 300;      % K
Tc  = 290;      % K

h  = 0.25;
t0 = 0;
tf = 1.0;

CA0 = 1.2;
T0  = 295;

t = t0:h:tf;
N = length(t);

U = zeros(2,N);
U(:,1) = [CA0; T0];

% U(1) = CA, U(2) = T
rate_constant = @(T) 0.6*exp(0.03*(T - 300));

f = @(t,U) [ ...
    (CAf - U(1))/tau - rate_constant(U(2))*U(1); ...
    (Tf - U(2))/tau + 18*rate_constant(U(2))*U(1) - 0.4*(U(2) - Tc) ...
    ];

k1_store = zeros(2,N-1);
k2_store = zeros(2,N-1);
k3_store = zeros(2,N-1);
k4_store = zeros(2,N-1);

for n = 1:N-1

    k1 = f(t(n), U(:,n));

    k2 = f(t(n) + h/2, U(:,n) + (h/2)*k1);

    k3 = f(t(n) + h/2, U(:,n) + (h/2)*k2);

    k4 = f(t(n) + h, U(:,n) + h*k3);

    U(:,n+1) = U(:,n) + (h/6)*(k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4);

    k1_store(:,n) = k1;
    k2_store(:,n) = k2;
    k3_store(:,n) = k3;
    k4_store(:,n) = k4;

end

CA = U(1,:)';
Temp = U(2,:)';

Results = table(t', CA, Temp, ...
    'VariableNames', {'Time_min', 'CA_mol_L', 'Temperature_K'});

disp(Results)

fprintf('CA(1.0) = %.6f mol/L\n', CA(end));
fprintf('T(1.0)  = %.6f K\n', Temp(end));

figure;
plot(t,CA,'-o','LineWidth',2);
grid on;
xlabel('Time (min)');
ylabel('C_A (mol/L)');
title('Non-Isothermal CSTR Concentration Profile');

figure;
plot(t,Temp,'-s','LineWidth',2);
grid on;
xlabel('Time (min)');
ylabel('Temperature (K)');
title('Non-Isothermal CSTR Temperature Profile');
P12 2D FDM + Gauss-Seidel — Reactor Wall with Heat Generation

A square reactor wall section has steady two-dimensional conduction with uniform internal heat generation. The governing equation is

\[ \frac{\partial^2T}{\partial x^2} + \frac{\partial^2T}{\partial y^2} + \frac{\dot q}{k} = 0 \]

Use a uniform grid with \(\Delta x=\Delta y=0.1\;m\). There are \(3\times3\) interior nodes. The boundary temperatures are:

\[ T_L=120^\circ C,\qquad T_R=60^\circ C,\qquad T_B=80^\circ C,\qquad T_T=100^\circ C \]

The heat generation term gives \(\left(\dot q/k\right)h^2=4^\circ C\). Starting with all interior nodes equal to \(90^\circ C\), perform Gauss-Seidel iteration until the nodal values are essentially converged.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Given

\[ \Delta x=\Delta y=h=0.1 \] \[ T_L=120,\qquad T_R=60,\qquad T_B=80,\qquad T_T=100 \] \[ \left(\frac{\dot q}{k}\right)h^2=4 \]

For a square grid with equal spacing:

\[ \frac{T_E-2T_P+T_W}{h^2} + \frac{T_N-2T_P+T_S}{h^2} + \frac{\dot q}{k} = 0 \]

Multiply by \(h^2\):

\[ T_E+T_W+T_N+T_S-4T_P+ \left(\frac{\dot q}{k}\right)h^2 = 0 \] \[ T_P = \frac{T_E+T_W+T_N+T_S+4}{4} \]

Node Numbering

Let \(T_{ij}\) denote the interior node at column \(i\) and row \(j\), where \(i=1,2,3\) from left to right and \(j=1,2,3\) from bottom to top.

\[ \begin{matrix} T_{13} & T_{23} & T_{33}\\ T_{12} & T_{22} & T_{32}\\ T_{11} & T_{21} & T_{31} \end{matrix} \]

Finite-Difference Equations

\[ T_{11}=\frac{120+T_{21}+80+T_{12}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{21}=\frac{T_{11}+T_{31}+80+T_{22}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{31}=\frac{T_{21}+60+80+T_{32}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{12}=\frac{120+T_{22}+T_{11}+T_{13}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{22}=\frac{T_{12}+T_{32}+T_{21}+T_{23}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{32}=\frac{T_{22}+60+T_{31}+T_{33}+4}{4} \] \[ T_{13}=\frac{120+T_{23}+T_{12}+100+4}{4} \] \[ T_{23}=\frac{T_{13}+T_{33}+T_{22}+100+4}{4} \] \[ T_{33}=\frac{T_{23}+60+T_{32}+100+4}{4} \]

Initial Guess

\[ T_{ij}^{(0)}=90^\circ C \qquad \text{for all interior nodes} \]

Iteration 1

Using Gauss-Seidel, each new value is used immediately in the next calculation.

\[ T_{11}^{(1)} = \frac{120+90+80+90+4}{4} = 96.0000 \] \[ T_{21}^{(1)} = \frac{96.0000+90+80+90+4}{4} = 90.0000 \] \[ T_{31}^{(1)} = \frac{90.0000+60+80+90+4}{4} = 81.0000 \] \[ T_{12}^{(1)} = \frac{120+90+96.0000+90+4}{4} = 100.0000 \] \[ T_{22}^{(1)} = \frac{100.0000+90+90.0000+90+4}{4} = 93.5000 \] \[ T_{32}^{(1)} = \frac{93.5000+60+81.0000+90+4}{4} = 82.1250 \] \[ T_{13}^{(1)} = \frac{120+90+100.0000+100+4}{4} = 103.5000 \] \[ T_{23}^{(1)} = \frac{103.5000+90+93.5000+100+4}{4} = 97.7500 \] \[ T_{33}^{(1)} = \frac{97.7500+60+82.1250+100+4}{4} = 85.9688 \]

Gauss-Seidel Iteration Table

Each matrix is shown from top row to bottom row.

\[ \text{Iteration 1:} \quad \begin{bmatrix} 103.5000 & 97.7500 & 85.9688\\ 100.0000 & 93.5000 & 82.1250\\ 96.0000 & 90.0000 & 81.0000 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \text{Iteration 2:} \quad \begin{bmatrix} 106.6562 & 97.7812 & 85.6523\\ 104.8750 & 94.5000 & 80.8281\\ 98.5000 & 89.2500 & 78.8438 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \text{Iteration 3:} \quad \begin{bmatrix} 106.9883 & 97.7852 & 85.6128\\ 106.1719 & 94.5000 & 80.6660\\ 99.5312 & 89.2188 & 78.5117 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \text{Iteration 4:} \quad \begin{bmatrix} 107.0298 & 97.7856 & 85.6078\\ 106.3340 & 94.5000 & 80.6458\\ 99.8477 & 89.2148 & 78.4702 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \text{Iteration 5:} \quad \begin{bmatrix} 107.0350 & 97.7857 & 85.6072\\ 106.3542 & 94.5000 & 80.6432\\ 99.8872 & 89.2144 & 78.4650 \end{bmatrix} \]

Converged Temperature Field

\[ \begin{bmatrix} T_{13} & T_{23} & T_{33}\\ T_{12} & T_{22} & T_{32}\\ T_{11} & T_{21} & T_{31} \end{bmatrix} = \begin{bmatrix} 107.0357 & 97.7857 & 85.6071\\ 106.3571 & 94.5000 & 80.6429\\ 99.8929 & 89.2143 & 78.4643 \end{bmatrix} \]

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{ T_{11}=99.8929,\quad T_{21}=89.2143,\quad T_{31}=78.4643 } \] \[ \boxed{ T_{12}=106.3571,\quad T_{22}=94.5000,\quad T_{32}=80.6429 } \] \[ \boxed{ T_{13}=107.0357,\quad T_{23}=97.7857,\quad T_{33}=85.6071 } \]

The highest interior temperature occurs near the left and upper boundaries because those boundaries are hotter, and the internal heat generation adds heat throughout the wall.

▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P12 2D FDM with Gauss-Seidel

2D Reactor Wall Heat Generation — FDM + Gauss-Seidel
%% P12 — 2D FDM + Gauss-Seidel: Reactor Wall with Heat Generation

clc;
clear;
close all;

% Boundary temperatures, deg C
TL = 120;
TR = 60;
TB = 80;
TT = 100;

% Heat generation term: (qdot/k)*h^2
Q = 4;

% Number of interior nodes in x and y directions
Nx = 3;
Ny = 3;

% Initial guess
T = 90*ones(Ny,Nx);

tol = 1e-6;
maxIter = 100;

Error = zeros(maxIter,1);

for iter = 1:maxIter

    Told = T;

    for j = 1:Ny
        for i = 1:Nx

            % West neighbor
            if i == 1
                TW = TL;
            else
                TW = T(j,i-1);
            end

            % East neighbor
            if i == Nx
                TE = TR;
            else
                TE = T(j,i+1);
            end

            % South neighbor
            if j == 1
                TS = TB;
            else
                TS = T(j-1,i);
            end

            % North neighbor
            if j == Ny
                TN = TT;
            else
                TN = T(j+1,i);
            end

            % Gauss-Seidel update
            T(j,i) = (TW + TE + TS + TN + Q)/4;

        end
    end

    Error(iter) = max(max(abs(T - Told)));

    if Error(iter) < tol
        Error = Error(1:iter);
        break;
    end

end

% Display matrix from top row to bottom row
T_display = flipud(T);

disp('Converged interior temperature matrix, top row to bottom row:')
disp(T_display)

fprintf('Number of iterations = %d\n', iter);
fprintf('Maximum final error = %.6e\n', Error(end));

% Build coordinate grid for plotting
x = 1:Nx;
y = 1:Ny;

figure;
surf(x,y,T);
grid on;
xlabel('Interior x-index');
ylabel('Interior y-index');
zlabel('Temperature (deg C)');
title('2D FDM Temperature Field with Heat Generation');

figure;
contourf(x,y,T,20);
colorbar;
xlabel('Interior x-index');
ylabel('Interior y-index');
title('2D Reactor Wall Temperature Contours');
P13 2D FDM + Gauss-Jordan — Advanced Anisotropic Catalytic Reactor Wall

A thin catalytic reactor wall has anisotropic conduction, internal heat generation, and distributed coolant heat removal. The steady-state temperature field is governed by

\[ k_x\frac{\partial^2 T}{\partial x^2} +k_y\frac{\partial^2 T}{\partial y^2} -U_v(T-T_c)+q'''=0 \]

where

\[ k_x=12\;\frac{W}{m\cdot K},\qquad k_y=4\;\frac{W}{m\cdot K},\qquad U_v=60\;\frac{W}{m^3\cdot K} \] \[ T_c=300\;K, \qquad q'''=12000\;\frac{W}{m^3} \]

The square wall has dimensions

\[ 0\le x\le 0.30\;m, \qquad 0\le y\le 0.30\;m \]

with boundary temperatures

\[ T(0,y)=380\;K, \qquad T(0.30,y)=320\;K \] \[ T(x,0)=350\;K, \qquad T(x,0.30)=300\;K \]

Use a uniform grid with \(\Delta x=\Delta y=0.075\;m\), giving nine interior unknown temperatures. Set up the complete 2D FDM system and solve it using Gauss-Jordan elimination.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1: Physical Model

\[ k_x\frac{\partial^2T}{\partial x^2} +k_y\frac{\partial^2T}{\partial y^2} -U_v(T-T_c)+q'''=0 \]

The central-difference approximations are

\[ \frac{\partial^2T}{\partial x^2} \approx \frac{T_E-2T_P+T_W}{\Delta x^2} \] \[ \frac{\partial^2T}{\partial y^2} \approx \frac{T_N-2T_P+T_S}{\Delta y^2} \]

Substitute into the PDE:

\[ k_x\frac{T_E-2T_P+T_W}{\Delta x^2} +k_y\frac{T_N-2T_P+T_S}{\Delta y^2} -U_v(T_P-T_c)+q'''=0 \]

Step 2: Define FDM Coefficients

\[ \Delta x=\Delta y=0.075 \] \[ \Delta x^2=\Delta y^2=0.005625 \] \[ a_x=\frac{k_x}{\Delta x^2} =\frac{12}{0.005625}=2133.3333 \] \[ a_y=\frac{k_y}{\Delta y^2} =\frac{4}{0.005625}=711.1111 \]

The unscaled node equation is

\[ (2a_x+2a_y+U_v)T_P -a_xT_W-a_xT_E-a_yT_S-a_yT_N =U_vT_c+q''' \] \[ U_vT_c+q'''=60(300)+12000=30000 \]

Divide the full equation by \(a_y=711.1111\) to make the algebra cleaner:

\[ r=\frac{a_x}{a_y}=3 \] \[ \lambda=\frac{U_v}{a_y}=\frac{60}{711.1111}=0.084375 \] \[ Q=\frac{U_vT_c+q'''}{a_y} =\frac{30000}{711.1111}=42.1875 \] \[ D=2r+2+\lambda =2(3)+2+0.084375 =8.084375 \]

Therefore, every interior node satisfies

\[ \boxed{ 8.084375T_P-3T_W-3T_E-T_S-T_N=42.1875 } \]

Step 3: Grid and Unknown Numbering

There are 3 interior nodes in each direction:

\[ x=0.075,\;0.150,\;0.225 \] \[ y=0.075,\;0.150,\;0.225 \]

Use the unknown vector

\[ \mathbf{T}= \begin{bmatrix} T_{11}\\T_{21}\\T_{31}\\ T_{12}\\T_{22}\\T_{32}\\ T_{13}\\T_{23}\\T_{33} \end{bmatrix} \]

where \(T_{ij}\) means the node at x-index \(i\) and y-index \(j\). The index \(j=1\) is the bottom interior row.

Step 4: Write the Nine FDM Equations

Boundary values are moved to the right-hand side.

Bottom-left node \(T_{11}\)
\[ 8.084375T_{11}-3T_{21}-T_{12} =42.1875+3(380)+350 \] \[ 8.084375T_{11}-3T_{21}-T_{12}=1532.1875 \]
Bottom-middle node \(T_{21}\)
\[ -3T_{11}+8.084375T_{21}-3T_{31}-T_{22} =42.1875+350 \] \[ -3T_{11}+8.084375T_{21}-3T_{31}-T_{22}=392.1875 \]
Bottom-right node \(T_{31}\)
\[ -3T_{21}+8.084375T_{31}-T_{32} =42.1875+3(320)+350 \] \[ -3T_{21}+8.084375T_{31}-T_{32}=1352.1875 \]
Middle-left node \(T_{12}\)
\[ -T_{11}+8.084375T_{12}-3T_{22}-T_{13} =42.1875+3(380) \] \[ -T_{11}+8.084375T_{12}-3T_{22}-T_{13}=1182.1875 \]
Center node \(T_{22}\)
\[ -T_{21}-3T_{12}+8.084375T_{22}-3T_{32}-T_{23} =42.1875 \]
Middle-right node \(T_{32}\)
\[ -T_{31}-3T_{22}+8.084375T_{32}-T_{33} =42.1875+3(320) \] \[ -T_{31}-3T_{22}+8.084375T_{32}-T_{33}=1002.1875 \]
Top-left node \(T_{13}\)
\[ -T_{12}+8.084375T_{13}-3T_{23} =42.1875+3(380)+300 \] \[ -T_{12}+8.084375T_{13}-3T_{23}=1482.1875 \]
Top-middle node \(T_{23}\)
\[ -T_{22}-3T_{13}+8.084375T_{23}-3T_{33} =42.1875+300 \] \[ -T_{22}-3T_{13}+8.084375T_{23}-3T_{33}=342.1875 \]
Top-right node \(T_{33}\)
\[ -T_{32}-3T_{23}+8.084375T_{33} =42.1875+3(320)+300 \] \[ -T_{32}-3T_{23}+8.084375T_{33}=1302.1875 \]

Step 5: Matrix Form

\[ \begin{bmatrix} 8.084375&-3&0&-1&0&0&0&0&0\\ -3&8.084375&-3&0&-1&0&0&0&0\\ 0&-3&8.084375&0&0&-1&0&0&0\\ -1&0&0&8.084375&-3&0&-1&0&0\\ 0&-1&0&-3&8.084375&-3&0&-1&0\\ 0&0&-1&0&-3&8.084375&0&0&-1\\ 0&0&0&-1&0&0&8.084375&-3&0\\ 0&0&0&0&-1&0&-3&8.084375&-3\\ 0&0&0&0&0&-1&0&-3&8.084375 \end{bmatrix} \begin{bmatrix} T_{11}\\T_{21}\\T_{31}\\T_{12}\\T_{22}\\T_{32}\\T_{13}\\T_{23}\\T_{33} \end{bmatrix} = \begin{bmatrix} 1532.1875\\392.1875\\1352.1875\\1182.1875\\42.1875\\1002.1875\\1482.1875\\342.1875\\1302.1875 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 6: Gauss-Jordan Elimination

Start with the augmented matrix

\[ [A|b] \]

For pivot column \(k\), use

\[ R_k\leftarrow \frac{R_k}{a_{kk}} \]

then eliminate the pivot column from every other row:

\[ R_i\leftarrow R_i-a_{ik}R_k, \qquad i\ne k \]

After applying the operation for all nine pivot columns, the augmented matrix becomes

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccccccccc|c} 1&0&0&0&0&0&0&0&0&366.2940\\ 0&1&0&0&0&0&0&0&0&354.3388\\ 0&0&1&0&0&0&0&0&0&340.4850\\ 0&0&0&1&0&0&0&0&0&366.0545\\ 0&0&0&0&1&0&0&0&0&352.0830\\ 0&0&0&0&0&1&0&0&0&337.4044\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&1&0&0&354.5911\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&0&1&0&339.4684\\ 0&0&0&0&0&0&0&0&1&328.7820 \end{array} \right] \]

Step 7: Interior Temperature Results

\[ T_{11}=366.2940\;K \] \[ T_{21}=354.3388\;K \] \[ T_{31}=340.4850\;K \] \[ T_{12}=366.0545\;K \] \[ T_{22}=352.0830\;K \] \[ T_{32}=337.4044\;K \] \[ T_{13}=354.5911\;K \] \[ T_{23}=339.4684\;K \] \[ T_{33}=328.7820\;K \]

Written as a 2D interior temperature matrix from top row to bottom row:

\[ \boxed{ T_{interior}= \begin{bmatrix} 354.5911&339.4684&328.7820\\ 366.0545&352.0830&337.4044\\ 366.2940&354.3388&340.4850 \end{bmatrix}K } \]

Engineering Interpretation

The hottest interior region is near the left and bottom boundaries because those surfaces are held at higher temperatures. The right and top sides are cooler, so temperature decreases toward the upper-right corner. The anisotropic conductivity makes x-direction coupling three times stronger than y-direction coupling, which is why temperatures smooth more strongly from left to right than from bottom to top.

▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P13 2D FDM with Gauss-Jordan Elimination

Advanced 2D FDM Reactor Wall — Explicit Gauss-Jordan Solver
%% P13 — Advanced 2D FDM with Gauss-Jordan Elimination

clc;
clear;
close all;

%% Problem data
kx = 12;              % W/(m K)
ky = 4;               % W/(m K)
Uv = 60;              % W/(m^3 K)
Tc = 300;             % K
qgen = 12000;         % W/m^3

Lx = 0.30;            % m
Ly = 0.30;            % m

TL = 380;             % left boundary, K
TR = 320;             % right boundary, K
TB = 350;             % bottom boundary, K
TT = 300;             % top boundary, K

Nx = 3;               % number of interior nodes in x
Ny = 3;               % number of interior nodes in y

N = Nx*Ny;            % total unknowns

dx = Lx/(Nx + 1);
dy = Ly/(Ny + 1);

%% FDM coefficients
ax = kx/dx^2;
ay = ky/dy^2;
D  = 2*ax + 2*ay + Uv;
rhs0 = Uv*Tc + qgen;

A = zeros(N,N);
b = zeros(N,1);

%% Node mapping:
% p = (j-1)*Nx + i
% i = 1,2,3 from left to right
% j = 1,2,3 from bottom to top

for j = 1:Ny
    for i = 1:Nx

        p = (j-1)*Nx + i;

        A(p,p) = D;
        b(p) = rhs0;

        % West neighbor
        if i == 1
            b(p) = b(p) + ax*TL;
        else
            pW = (j-1)*Nx + (i-1);
            A(p,pW) = -ax;
        end

        % East neighbor
        if i == Nx
            b(p) = b(p) + ax*TR;
        else
            pE = (j-1)*Nx + (i+1);
            A(p,pE) = -ax;
        end

        % South neighbor
        if j == 1
            b(p) = b(p) + ay*TB;
        else
            pS = (j-2)*Nx + i;
            A(p,pS) = -ay;
        end

        % North neighbor
        if j == Ny
            b(p) = b(p) + ay*TT;
        else
            pN = j*Nx + i;
            A(p,pN) = -ay;
        end

    end
end

%% Scale the system for cleaner Gauss-Jordan arithmetic
As = A/ay;
bs = b/ay;
Aug = [As bs];

fprintf('Scaled coefficient matrix [A]:\n')
disp(As)

fprintf('Scaled right-hand side [b]:\n')
disp(bs)

%% Gauss-Jordan elimination with partial pivoting
for k = 1:N

    % Partial pivoting
    [~, pivotRow] = max(abs(Aug(k:N,k)));
    pivotRow = pivotRow + k - 1;

    if pivotRow ~= k
        temp = Aug(k,:);
        Aug(k,:) = Aug(pivotRow,:);
        Aug(pivotRow,:) = temp;
    end

    % Normalize pivot row
    pivot = Aug(k,k);

    if abs(pivot) < 1e-12
        error('Zero or near-zero pivot detected. System cannot be solved safely.');
    end

    Aug(k,:) = Aug(k,:)/pivot;

    % Eliminate pivot column from every other row
    for i = 1:N
        if i ~= k
            factor = Aug(i,k);
            Aug(i,:) = Aug(i,:) - factor*Aug(k,:);
        end
    end

    fprintf('\nAugmented matrix after pivot column %d:\n', k)
    disp(Aug)

end

%% Extract solution
Tvec = Aug(:,end);

% Convert vector to 2D matrix.
% Tmat row 1 is bottom interior row.
Tmat = reshape(Tvec,Nx,Ny)';
TtopToBottom = flipud(Tmat);

Residual = As*Tvec - bs;

fprintf('\nFinal reduced row echelon form [I | T]:\n')
disp(Aug)

fprintf('\nInterior temperatures, vector order:\n')
disp(Tvec)

fprintf('\nInterior temperature matrix, top row to bottom row:\n')
disp(TtopToBottom)

fprintf('\nMaximum absolute residual = %.6e\n', max(abs(Residual)))

%% Plot interior temperature field
xInterior = dx:dx:(Lx-dx);
yInterior = dy:dy:(Ly-dy);

[Xgrid,Ygrid] = meshgrid(xInterior,yInterior);

figure;
surf(Xgrid,Ygrid,Tmat);
grid on;
xlabel('x (m)');
ylabel('y (m)');
zlabel('Temperature (K)');
title('P13: 2D FDM Interior Temperature Field');

figure;
contourf(Xgrid,Ygrid,Tmat,20);
colorbar;
xlabel('x (m)');
ylabel('y (m)');
title('P13: 2D FDM Temperature Contours');
P14 Regression — Quadratic Least-Squares Fit with Gauss-Jordan

Experimental adsorption data were collected for a solute on an activated carbon surface. The equilibrium loading \(q\) changes nonlinearly with concentration \(C\).

\(C\) (mol/L) \(q\) (mol/kg)
02.1
13.9
27.2
311.9
418.1
525.8

Fit the quadratic regression model:

\[ q=a_0+a_1C+a_2C^2 \]

Use the least-squares normal equations and solve the matrix using Gauss-Jordan elimination.

▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1 — Regression Model

\[ q=a_0+a_1C+a_2C^2 \]

The unknown regression coefficients are:

\[ a_0,\qquad a_1,\qquad a_2 \]

Since there are 6 data points and only 3 unknown coefficients, the curve will not necessarily pass through every data point. Instead, we minimize:

\[ SSE=\sum_{i=1}^{6} \left(q_i-a_0-a_1C_i-a_2C_i^2\right)^2 \]

Step 2 — Build the Least-Squares Table

For quadratic regression, the normal equations require:

\[ \sum C,\quad \sum C^2,\quad \sum C^3,\quad \sum C^4,\quad \sum q,\quad \sum Cq,\quad \sum C^2q \]
\(C\) \(q\) \(C^2\) \(C^3\) \(C^4\) \(Cq\) \(C^2q\)
02.10000.00.0
13.91113.93.9
27.2481614.428.8
311.99278135.7107.1
418.1166425672.4289.6
525.825125625129.0645.0

Now sum each column:

\[ n=6 \] \[ \sum C=15 \] \[ \sum C^2=55 \] \[ \sum C^3=225 \] \[ \sum C^4=979 \] \[ \sum q=69.0 \] \[ \sum Cq=255.4 \] \[ \sum C^2q=1074.4 \]

Step 3 — Write the Normal Equations

For:

\[ q=a_0+a_1C+a_2C^2 \]

the normal equations are:

\[ \begin{aligned} na_0+a_1\sum C+a_2\sum C^2&=\sum q\\ a_0\sum C+a_1\sum C^2+a_2\sum C^3&=\sum Cq\\ a_0\sum C^2+a_1\sum C^3+a_2\sum C^4&=\sum C^2q \end{aligned} \]

Substitute the summations:

\[ \begin{aligned} 6a_0+15a_1+55a_2&=69.0\\ 15a_0+55a_1+225a_2&=255.4\\ 55a_0+225a_1+979a_2&=1074.4 \end{aligned} \]

Matrix form:

\[ \begin{bmatrix} 6&15&55\\ 15&55&225\\ 55&225&979 \end{bmatrix} \begin{bmatrix} a_0\\ a_1\\ a_2 \end{bmatrix} = \begin{bmatrix} 69.0\\ 255.4\\ 1074.4 \end{bmatrix} \]

Step 4 — Gauss-Jordan Setup

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccc|c} 6&15&55&69.0\\ 15&55&225&255.4\\ 55&225&979&1074.4 \end{array} \right] \]

Goal:

\[ [A|b]\rightarrow[I|a] \]

Step 5 — Pivot Column 1

Normalize Row 1:

\[ R_1\leftarrow \frac{1}{6}R_1 \] \[ R_1= [1,\;2.5,\;9.166667\;|\;11.5] \]

Eliminate \(a_0\) from Row 2:

\[ R_2\leftarrow R_2-15R_1 \] \[ R_2= [15,\;55,\;225\;|\;255.4] - 15[1,\;2.5,\;9.166667\;|\;11.5] \] \[ R_2= [0,\;17.5,\;87.5\;|\;82.9] \]

Eliminate \(a_0\) from Row 3:

\[ R_3\leftarrow R_3-55R_1 \] \[ R_3= [55,\;225,\;979\;|\;1074.4] - 55[1,\;2.5,\;9.166667\;|\;11.5] \] \[ R_3= [0,\;87.5,\;474.8333\;|\;441.9] \]

Matrix after Column 1:

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccc|c} 1&2.5&9.166667&11.5\\ 0&17.5&87.5&82.9\\ 0&87.5&474.8333&441.9 \end{array} \right] \]

Step 6 — Pivot Column 2

Normalize Row 2:

\[ R_2\leftarrow \frac{1}{17.5}R_2 \] \[ R_2=[0,\;1,\;5\;|\;4.737143] \]

Eliminate \(a_1\) from Row 1:

\[ R_1\leftarrow R_1-2.5R_2 \] \[ R_1= [1,\;2.5,\;9.166667\;|\;11.5] - 2.5[0,\;1,\;5\;|\;4.737143] \] \[ R_1=[1,\;0,\;-3.333333\;|\;-0.342857] \]

Eliminate \(a_1\) from Row 3:

\[ R_3\leftarrow R_3-87.5R_2 \] \[ R_3= [0,\;87.5,\;474.8333\;|\;441.9] - 87.5[0,\;1,\;5\;|\;4.737143] \] \[ R_3=[0,\;0,\;37.333333\;|\;27.4] \]

Matrix after Column 2:

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccc|c} 1&0&-3.333333&-0.342857\\ 0&1&5&4.737143\\ 0&0&37.333333&27.4 \end{array} \right] \]

Step 7 — Pivot Column 3

Normalize Row 3:

\[ R_3\leftarrow \frac{1}{37.333333}R_3 \] \[ R_3=[0,\;0,\;1\;|\;0.733929] \]

Therefore:

\[ a_2=0.733929 \]

Eliminate \(a_2\) from Row 1:

\[ R_1\leftarrow R_1+3.333333R_3 \] \[ R_1= [1,\;0,\;-3.333333\;|\;-0.342857] + 3.333333[0,\;0,\;1\;|\;0.733929] \] \[ R_1=[1,\;0,\;0\;|\;2.103571] \]

Eliminate \(a_2\) from Row 2:

\[ R_2\leftarrow R_2-5R_3 \] \[ R_2= [0,\;1,\;5\;|\;4.737143] - 5[0,\;0,\;1\;|\;0.733929] \] \[ R_2=[0,\;1,\;0\;|\;1.067500] \]

Step 8 — Final Reduced Matrix

\[ \left[ \begin{array}{ccc|c} 1&0&0&2.103571\\ 0&1&0&1.067500\\ 0&0&1&0.733929 \end{array} \right] \]

Step 9 — Final Regression Model

\[ a_0=2.103571 \] \[ a_1=1.067500 \] \[ a_2=0.733929 \] \[ \boxed{ q=2.103571+1.067500C+0.733929C^2 } \]

Step 10 — Residual Check

\(C\) Measured \(q\) Predicted \(q\) Residual
02.10002.1036-0.0036
13.90003.9050-0.0050
27.20007.17430.0257
311.900011.9114-0.0114
418.100018.1164-0.0164
525.800025.78930.0107
\[ SSE=0.001214 \] \[ R^2=0.999997 \]
The quadratic model fits the adsorption data extremely well because the residuals are very small and \(R^2\) is almost 1.
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P13 Quadratic Regression with Gauss-Jordan

Quadratic Least-Squares Regression
%% P13 — Quadratic Regression using Gauss-Jordan Elimination
% Model:
%     q = a0 + a1*C + a2*C^2
%
% The normal equations are solved manually using Gauss-Jordan elimination.

clc;
clear;
close all;

%% Experimental data

C = [0; 1; 2; 3; 4; 5];
q = [2.1; 3.9; 7.2; 11.9; 18.1; 25.8];

%% Build normal equation matrix

n = length(C);

Sx   = sum(C);
Sx2  = sum(C.^2);
Sx3  = sum(C.^3);
Sx4  = sum(C.^4);

Sy   = sum(q);
Sxy  = sum(C.*q);
Sx2y = sum((C.^2).*q);

A = [n,   Sx,  Sx2;
     Sx,  Sx2, Sx3;
     Sx2, Sx3, Sx4];

b = [Sy; Sxy; Sx2y];

%% Gauss-Jordan elimination

Aug = [A b];

m = length(b);

for k = 1:m

    % Normalize pivot row
    Aug(k,:) = Aug(k,:) / Aug(k,k);

    % Eliminate pivot variable from all other rows
    for i = 1:m
        if i ~= k
            factor = Aug(i,k);
            Aug(i,:) = Aug(i,:) - factor*Aug(k,:);
        end
    end

    fprintf('Matrix after pivot column %d:\n', k)
    disp(Aug)

end

coeff = Aug(:,end);

a0 = coeff(1);
a1 = coeff(2);
a2 = coeff(3);

%% Predictions and errors

q_pred = a0 + a1*C + a2*C.^2;

residual = q - q_pred;

SSE = sum(residual.^2);
SST = sum((q - mean(q)).^2);
R2 = 1 - SSE/SST;

Results = table(C, q, q_pred, residual, ...
    'VariableNames', {'C', 'q_measured', 'q_predicted', 'Residual'});

disp('Quadratic Regression Results:')
disp(Results)

fprintf('a0 = %.6f\n', a0)
fprintf('a1 = %.6f\n', a1)
fprintf('a2 = %.6f\n', a2)
fprintf('SSE = %.6e\n', SSE)
fprintf('R2 = %.6f\n', R2)

%% Plot result

Cfine = linspace(min(C), max(C), 200)';
qfine = a0 + a1*Cfine + a2*Cfine.^2;

figure;
plot(C, q, 'o', 'LineWidth', 2);
hold on;
plot(Cfine, qfine, '-', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;

xlabel('Concentration C');
ylabel('Adsorption loading q');
title('Quadratic Least-Squares Regression');
legend('Experimental Data', 'Quadratic Fit', 'Location', 'best');
P15 Nonlinear Regression — Michaelis-Menten Parameter Estimation

An enzyme-catalyzed reaction follows Michaelis-Menten kinetics:

\[ v=\frac{V_{max}S}{K_m+S} \]

Experimental reaction-rate data are:

\(S\) (mol/L) \(v_{obs}\) (mol/L·min)
0.51.12
1.01.90
2.03.05
4.04.25
6.04.85
8.05.21

Use nonlinear least-squares regression with the Gauss-Newton method to estimate \(V_{max}\) and \(K_m\).

Initial guess:

\[ V_{max}^{(0)}=5.0000, \qquad K_m^{(0)}=1.0000 \]
▶ Reveal Detailed Answer

Step 1 — Define the Nonlinear Model

\[ v_{calc} = \frac{V_{max}S}{K_m+S} \]

The residual for each data point is:

\[ r_i=v_{obs,i}-v_{calc,i} \]

The objective is:

\[ SSE=\sum_{i=1}^{n}r_i^2 \]

Step 2 — Derivatives for Gauss-Newton

The Gauss-Newton method needs the sensitivity of the calculated rate with respect to each unknown parameter.

\[ v=\frac{V_{max}S}{K_m+S} \]

Derivative with respect to \(V_{max}\):

\[ \frac{\partial v}{\partial V_{max}} = \frac{S}{K_m+S} \]

Derivative with respect to \(K_m\):

\[ \frac{\partial v}{\partial K_m} = -\frac{V_{max}S}{(K_m+S)^2} \]

The Jacobian matrix is:

\[ J= \begin{bmatrix} \dfrac{\partial v_1}{\partial V_{max}} & \dfrac{\partial v_1}{\partial K_m}\\ \dfrac{\partial v_2}{\partial V_{max}} & \dfrac{\partial v_2}{\partial K_m}\\ \vdots & \vdots\\ \dfrac{\partial v_n}{\partial V_{max}} & \dfrac{\partial v_n}{\partial K_m} \end{bmatrix} \]

The Gauss-Newton correction is found from:

\[ (J^TJ)\Delta\theta=J^Tr \] where: \[ \Delta\theta= \begin{bmatrix} \Delta V_{max}\\ \Delta K_m \end{bmatrix} \]

Then:

\[ \theta_{new}=\theta_{old}+\Delta\theta \]

Iteration 0 — Use \(V_{max}=5.0000,\;K_m=1.0000\)

The model becomes:

\[ v_{calc}=\frac{5S}{1+S} \]
\(S\) \(v_{obs}\) \(v_{calc}\) \(r\) \(\partial v/\partial V_{max}\) \(\partial v/\partial K_m\)
0.51.121.6667-0.54670.3333-1.1111
1.01.902.5000-0.60000.5000-1.2500
2.03.053.3333-0.28330.6667-1.1111
4.04.254.00000.25000.8000-0.8000
6.04.854.28570.56430.8571-0.6122
8.05.214.44440.76560.8889-0.4938
\[ SSE^{(0)}=1.706116 \]

Form the normal equations:

\[ J^TJ= \begin{bmatrix} 2.9704 & -3.3398\\ -3.3398 & 5.2903 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ J^Tr= \begin{bmatrix} 0.6931\\ 0.7487 \end{bmatrix} \]

Solve:

\[ \begin{bmatrix} 2.9704 & -3.3398\\ -3.3398 & 5.2903 \end{bmatrix} \begin{bmatrix} \Delta V_{max}\\ \Delta K_m \end{bmatrix} = \begin{bmatrix} 0.6931\\ 0.7487 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \Delta V_{max}=1.3525 \] \[ \Delta K_m=0.9954 \]

Update:

\[ V_{max}^{(1)}=5.0000+1.3525=6.3525 \] \[ K_m^{(1)}=1.0000+0.9954=1.9954 \]

Iteration 1 — Use \(V_{max}=6.3525,\;K_m=1.9954\)

\[ v_{calc}= \frac{6.3525S}{1.9954+S} \]

4.04.254.23830.01170.6672-0.7069
6.04.854.76710.08290.7504-0.5962
8.05.215.08440.12560.8004-0.5087
\[ SSE^{(1)}=0.111779 \]

The error dropped sharply from \(1.706116\) to \(0.111779\).

\[ J^TJ= \begin{bmatrix} 2.0511 & -2.0632\\ -2.0632 & 2.5089 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ J^Tr= \begin{bmatrix} 0.0012\\ 0.2161 \end{bmatrix} \]

Solving the correction system gives:

\[ \Delta V_{max}=0.5048 \] \[ \Delta K_m=0.5012 \]

Update:

\[ V_{max}^{(2)}=6.3525+0.5048=6.8573 \] \[ K_m^{(2)}=1.9954+0.5012=2.4966 \]

\[ v_{calc} = \frac{6.8573S}{2.4966+S} \]

\[ SSE^{(2)}=0.005425 \] \[ J^TJ= \begin{bmatrix} 1.7661 & -1.7079\\ -1.7079 & 1.9155 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ J^Tr= \begin{bmatrix} -0.0113\\ 0.0291 \end{bmatrix} \]

Solving gives:

Since both corrections are extremely small, the regression has converged.

▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P14 Nonlinear Regression with Gauss-Newton

Michaelis-Menten Parameter Estimation
%% P14 — Nonlinear Regression using Gauss-Newton Method
% Model:
%     v = Vmax*S/(Km + S)
%
% Unknown parameters:
%     Vmax and Km
%
% Gauss-Newton equation:
%     (J'*J)*delta = J'*r

clc;
clear;
close all;

%% Experimental data

S = [0.5; 1; 2; 4; 6; 8];

vobs = [1.12; 1.90; 3.05; 4.25; 4.85; 5.21];

%% Initial guesses

Vmax = 5.0;
Km = 1.0;

tol = 1e-6;
maxIter = 20;

history = [];

%% Gauss-Newton iteration

for iter = 0:maxIter

    % Model prediction
    vcalc = Vmax*S./(Km + S);

    % Residual vector
    r = vobs - vcalc;

    % Sum of squared errors
    SSE = sum(r.^2);

    % Jacobian matrix
    dVmax = S./(Km + S);
    dKm = -Vmax*S./(Km + S).^2;

    J = [dVmax, dKm];

    % Solve the Gauss-Newton normal equations
    delta = (J'*J)\(J'*r);

    dV = delta(1);
    dK = delta(2);

    history = [history; iter, Vmax, Km, SSE, dV, dK];

    fprintf('Iteration %d\n', iter)
    fprintf('Vmax = %.8f, Km = %.8f, SSE = %.8e\n', Vmax, Km, SSE)
    fprintf('dVmax = %.8e, dKm = %.8e\n\n', dV, dK)

    % Stop if corrections are very small
    if max(abs(delta)) < tol
        break
    end

    % Update parameters
    Vmax = Vmax + dV;
    Km = Km + dK;

end

%% Final predictions

vfit = Vmax*S./(Km + S);
residual = vobs - vfit;

SSE_final = sum(residual.^2);
RMSE = sqrt(SSE_final/(length(S)-2));

Results = table(S, vobs, vfit, residual, ...
    'VariableNames', {'S', 'v_observed', 'v_calculated', 'Residual'});

disp('Final Regression Table:')
disp(Results)

Convergence = array2table(history, ...
    'VariableNames', ...
    {'Iteration', 'Vmax', 'Km', 'SSE', 'Delta_Vmax', 'Delta_Km'});

disp('Gauss-Newton Convergence History:')
disp(Convergence)

fprintf('Final Vmax = %.6f\n', Vmax)
fprintf('Final Km = %.6f\n', Km)
fprintf('Final SSE = %.6e\n', SSE_final)
fprintf('Final RMSE = %.6f\n', RMSE)

%% Plot fitted curve

Sfine = linspace(min(S), max(S), 200)';
vfine = Vmax*Sfine./(Km + Sfine);

figure;
plot(S, vobs, 'o', 'LineWidth', 2);
hold on;
plot(Sfine, vfine, '-', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;

xlabel('Substrate concentration S');
ylabel('Reaction rate v');
title('Michaelis-Menten Nonlinear Regression');
legend('Experimental Data', 'Gauss-Newton Fit', 'Location', 'best');

%% Plot SSE convergence

figure;
semilogy(history(:,1), history(:,4), '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;

xlabel('Iteration');
ylabel('SSE');
title('Gauss-Newton SSE Convergence');
P16 Coupled ODE System — Batch Reactor \(A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C\)

A batch reactor contains a consecutive reaction system. Species \(A\) converts to desired intermediate \(B\), while \(B\) also undergoes nonlinear disappearance to final product \(C\).

\[ A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C \]

The governing ODE system is:

\[ \frac{dC_A}{dt}=-0.8C_A \] \[ \frac{dC_B}{dt}=0.8C_A-0.3C_B-0.15C_B^2 \]

Initial conditions:

\[ C_A(0)=2.0,\qquad C_B(0)=0 \]

Use RK4 with:

\[ h=0.2 \]

Find \(C_A(1.0)\) and \(C_B(1.0)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Hand-Writing Answer

Step 1 — Define the Vector Form

\[ \mathbf{Y} = \begin{bmatrix} C_A\\ C_B \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{Y}' = \mathbf{f}(t,\mathbf{Y}) = \begin{bmatrix} -0.8C_A\\ 0.8C_A-0.3C_B-0.15C_B^2 \end{bmatrix} \]

Classical RK4 for a system is:

\[ \mathbf{k}_1=\mathbf{f}(t_n,\mathbf{Y}_n) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+\frac{h}{2}, \mathbf{Y}_n+\frac{h}{2}\mathbf{k}_1\right) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+\frac{h}{2}, \mathbf{Y}_n+\frac{h}{2}\mathbf{k}_2\right) \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4=\mathbf{f}\left(t_n+h, \mathbf{Y}_n+h\mathbf{k}_3\right) \] \[ \mathbf{Y}_{n+1} = \mathbf{Y}_n+ \frac{h}{6} \left( \mathbf{k}_1+2\mathbf{k}_2+2\mathbf{k}_3+\mathbf{k}_4 \right) \]

Step 2 — First RK4 Step: \(t=0 \rightarrow 0.2\)

\[ C_A^0=2.0000,\qquad C_B^0=0.0000 \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_1\):

\[ k_{1,A}=-0.8(2.0000)=-1.6000 \] \[ k_{1,B}=0.8(2.0000)-0.3(0)-0.15(0)^2=1.6000 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -1.6000\\ 1.6000 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_2\):

\[ C_A=2.0000+\frac{0.2}{2}(-1.6000)=1.8400 \] \[ C_B=0+\frac{0.2}{2}(1.6000)=0.1600 \] \[ k_{2,A}=-0.8(1.8400)=-1.4720 \] \[ k_{2,B}=0.8(1.8400)-0.3(0.1600)-0.15(0.1600)^2 \] \[ k_{2,B}=1.4720-0.0480-0.00384=1.42016 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -1.4720\\ 1.42016 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_3\):

\[ C_A=2.0000+\frac{0.2}{2}(-1.4720)=1.8528 \] \[ C_B=0+\frac{0.2}{2}(1.42016)=0.142016 \] \[ k_{3,A}=-0.8(1.8528)=-1.48224 \] \[ k_{3,B}=0.8(1.8528)-0.3(0.142016)-0.15(0.142016)^2 \] \[ k_{3,B}=1.48224-0.042605-0.003025=1.43661 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -1.48224\\ 1.43661 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_4\):

\[ C_A=2.0000+0.2(-1.48224)=1.703552 \] \[ C_B=0+0.2(1.43661)=0.287322 \] \[ k_{4,A}=-0.8(1.703552)=-1.36284 \] \[ k_{4,B}=0.8(1.703552)-0.3(0.287322)-0.15(0.287322)^2 \] \[ k_{4,B}=1.362842-0.086197-0.012383=1.26426 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -1.36284\\ 1.26426 \end{bmatrix} \]

Update:

\[ C_A^1 = 2+\frac{0.2}{6} [-1.6000+2(-1.4720)+2(-1.48224)-1.36284] \] \[ C_A^1=1.70429 \] \[ C_B^1 = 0+\frac{0.2}{6} [1.6000+2(1.42016)+2(1.43661)+1.26426] \] \[ C_B^1=0.28593 \] \[ \boxed{ C_A(0.2)=1.70429,\qquad C_B(0.2)=0.28593 } \]

Step 3 — Second RK4 Step: \(t=0.2 \rightarrow 0.4\)

\[ C_A^1=1.70429,\qquad C_B^1=0.28593 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -1.36343\\ 1.26539 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -1.25436\\ 1.10510 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -1.26308\\ 1.12058 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -1.16134\\ 0.96930 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^2 = 1.70429+\frac{0.2}{6} [-1.36343+2(-1.25436)+2(-1.26308)-1.16134] \] \[ C_A^2=1.45230 \] \[ C_B^2 = 0.28593+\frac{0.2}{6} [1.26539+2(1.10510)+2(1.12058)+0.96930] \] \[ C_B^2=0.50879 \]

Step 4 — Third RK4 Step: \(t=0.4 \rightarrow 0.6\)

\[ C_A^2=1.45230,\qquad C_B^2=0.50879 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -1.16184\\ 0.97037 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -1.06889\\ 0.83209 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -1.07633\\ 0.84616 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.98963\\ 0.71726 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^3 = 1.45230+\frac{0.2}{6} [-1.16184+2(-1.06889)+2(-1.07633)-0.98963] \] \[ C_A^3=1.23757 \] \[ C_B^3 = 0.50879+\frac{0.2}{6} [0.97037+2(0.83209)+2(0.84616)+0.71726] \] \[ C_B^3=0.67693 \]

Step 5 — Fourth RK4 Step: \(t=0.6 \rightarrow 0.8\)

\[ C_A^3=1.23757,\qquad C_B^3=0.67693 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -0.99006\\ 0.71824 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -0.91085\\ 0.60213 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -0.91719\\ 0.61454 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.84331\\ 0.50739 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^4=1.05459 \] \[ C_B^4=0.79890 \]

Step 6 — Fifth RK4 Step: \(t=0.8 \rightarrow 1.0\)

\[ C_A^4=1.05459,\qquad C_B^4=0.79890 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} -0.84367\\ 0.50827 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} -0.77618\\ 0.41296 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} -0.78158\\ 0.42363 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} -0.71862\\ 0.33641 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^5 = 1.05459+\frac{0.2}{6} [-0.84367+2(-0.77618)+2(-0.78158)-0.71862] \] \[ C_A^5=0.89866 \] \[ C_B^5 = 0.79890+\frac{0.2}{6} [0.50827+2(0.41296)+2(0.42363)+0.33641] \] \[ C_B^5=0.88283 \]

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{ C_A(1.0)=0.89866 } \] \[ \boxed{ C_B(1.0)=0.88283 } \]
