▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P16 Coupled RK4 Reactor System

Batch Reactor \(A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C\)
%% P16 — Coupled ODE System using RK4
% Reaction system:
%     A -> B -> C
%
% ODEs:
%     dCA/dt = -0.8*CA
%     dCB/dt =  0.8*CA - 0.3*CB - 0.15*CB^2

clc;
clear;
close all;

h = 0.2;
t0 = 0;
tf = 1.0;

t = t0:h:tf;
N = length(t);

Y = zeros(2,N);

% Initial conditions
Y(:,1) = [2.0; 0.0];

% Function vector
f = @(t,Y) [ ...
    -0.8*Y(1); ...
     0.8*Y(1) - 0.3*Y(2) - 0.15*Y(2)^2 ];

% Storage for slopes
K1 = zeros(2,N-1);
K2 = zeros(2,N-1);
K3 = zeros(2,N-1);
K4 = zeros(2,N-1);

for n = 1:N-1

    K1(:,n) = f(t(n), Y(:,n));

    K2(:,n) = f(t(n)+h/2, Y(:,n)+(h/2)*K1(:,n));

    K3(:,n) = f(t(n)+h/2, Y(:,n)+(h/2)*K2(:,n));

    K4(:,n) = f(t(n)+h, Y(:,n)+h*K3(:,n));

    Y(:,n+1) = Y(:,n) + (h/6)*(K1(:,n)+2*K2(:,n)+2*K3(:,n)+K4(:,n));

end

CA = Y(1,:)';
CB = Y(2,:)';

Results = table(t', CA, CB, ...
    'VariableNames', {'Time', 'CA', 'CB'});

disp(Results)

fprintf('CA(1.0) = %.6f\n', CA(end))
fprintf('CB(1.0) = %.6f\n', CB(end))

figure;
plot(t, CA, '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
hold on;
plot(t, CB, '-s', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;

xlabel('Time');
ylabel('Concentration');
title('Coupled Batch Reactor ODE System using RK4');
legend('C_A', 'C_B', 'Location', 'best');
P17 Non-Isothermal ODE System — CSTR Start-Up with Heat Generation

A non-isothermal CSTR is started from an initial concentration and temperature. The concentration changes due to inlet flow and second-order reaction. The temperature changes due to inlet flow, heat generation, and cooling.

The coupled ODE model is:

\[ \frac{dC_A}{dt}=3-C_A-0.25C_A^2 \] \[ \frac{dT}{dt}=440-1.4T+3C_A^2 \]

Initial conditions:

\[ C_A(0)=1.0,\qquad T(0)=300 \]

Use RK4 with:

\[ h=0.2 \]

Find \(C_A(1.0)\) and \(T(1.0)\).

▶ Reveal Detailed Hand-Writing Answer

Step 1 — Define the Vector Form

\[ \mathbf{Y} = \begin{bmatrix} C_A\\ T \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{Y}' = \mathbf{f}(t,\mathbf{Y}) = \begin{bmatrix} 3-C_A-0.25C_A^2\\ 440-1.4T+3C_A^2 \end{bmatrix} \]

Notice that this is a coupled nonlinear system: concentration affects temperature through the term \(3C_A^2\).

Step 2 — First RK4 Step: \(t=0 \rightarrow 0.2\)

\[ C_A^0=1.0000,\qquad T^0=300.0000 \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_1\):

\[ k_{1,C}=3-1-0.25(1)^2=1.7500 \] \[ k_{1,T}=440-1.4(300)+3(1)^2 \] \[ k_{1,T}=440-420+3=23.0000 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 1.7500\\ 23.0000 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_2\):

\[ C_A=1+\frac{0.2}{2}(1.7500)=1.1750 \] \[ T=300+\frac{0.2}{2}(23.0000)=302.3000 \] \[ k_{2,C}=3-1.1750-0.25(1.1750)^2 \] \[ k_{2,C}=1.47984 \] \[ k_{2,T}=440-1.4(302.3000)+3(1.1750)^2 \] \[ k_{2,T}=20.92188 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 1.47984\\ 20.92188 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_3\):

\[ C_A=1+\frac{0.2}{2}(1.47984)=1.14798 \] \[ T=300+\frac{0.2}{2}(20.92188)=302.09219 \] \[ k_{3,C}=3-1.14798-0.25(1.14798)^2=1.52255 \] \[ k_{3,T}=440-1.4(302.09219)+3(1.14798)^2=21.02454 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 1.52255\\ 21.02454 \end{bmatrix} \]

Compute \(\mathbf{k}_4\):

\[ C_A=1+0.2(1.52255)=1.30451 \] \[ T=300+0.2(21.02454)=304.20491 \] \[ k_{4,C}=3-1.30451-0.25(1.30451)^2=1.27005 \] \[ k_{4,T}=440-1.4(304.20491)+3(1.30451)^2=19.21837 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} 1.27005\\ 19.21837 \end{bmatrix} \]

Update:

\[ C_A^1 = 1+\frac{0.2}{6} [1.7500+2(1.47984)+2(1.52255)+1.27005] \] \[ C_A^1=1.30083 \] \[ T^1 = 300+\frac{0.2}{6} [23.0000+2(20.92188)+2(21.02454)+19.21837] \] \[ T^1=304.20371 \] \[ \boxed{ C_A(0.2)=1.30083,\qquad T(0.2)=304.20371 } \]

Step 3 — Second RK4 Step: \(t=0.2 \rightarrow 0.4\)

\[ C_A^1=1.30083,\qquad T^1=304.20371 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 1.27613\\ 19.19127 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 1.06145\\ 17.54937 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 1.09813\\ 17.59662 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} 0.90160\\ 16.12311 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^2 = 1.30083+\frac{0.2}{6} [1.27613+2(1.06145)+2(1.09813)+0.90160] \] \[ C_A^2=1.51739 \] \[ T^2 = 304.20371+\frac{0.2}{6} [19.19127+2(17.54937)+2(17.59662)+16.12311] \] \[ T^2=307.72392 \]

Step 4 — Third RK4 Step: \(t=0.4 \rightarrow 0.6\)

\[ C_A^2=1.51739,\qquad T^2=307.72392 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 0.90699\\ 16.09394 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 0.74542\\ 14.69122 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 0.77450\\ 14.73250 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} 0.62857\\ 13.45110 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^3=1.66990 \] \[ T^3=310.67033 \]

Step 5 — Fourth RK4 Step: \(t=0.6 \rightarrow 0.8\)

\[ C_A^3=1.66990,\qquad T^3=310.67033 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 0.63295\\ 13.42728 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 0.51580\\ 12.19366 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 0.53764\\ 12.24495 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} 0.43275\\ 11.11074 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^4=1.77566 \] \[ T^4=313.11751 \]

Step 6 — Fifth RK4 Step: \(t=0.8 \rightarrow 1.0\)

\[ C_A^4=1.77566,\qquad T^4=313.11751 \] \[ \mathbf{k}_1= \begin{bmatrix} 0.43610\\ 11.09437 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_2= \begin{bmatrix} 0.35330\\ 10.01148 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_3= \begin{bmatrix} 0.36909\\ 10.07291 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ \mathbf{k}_4= \begin{bmatrix} 0.29538\\ 9.07676 \end{bmatrix} \] \[ C_A^5 = 1.77566+ \frac{0.2}{6} [0.43610+2(0.35330)+2(0.36909)+0.29538] \] \[ C_A^5=1.84820 \] \[ T^5 = 313.11751+ \frac{0.2}{6} [11.09437+2(10.01148)+2(10.07291)+9.07676] \] \[ T^5=315.12884 \]

Final Answer

\[ \boxed{ C_A(1.0)=1.84820 } \] \[ \boxed{ T(1.0)=315.12884 } \]

The concentration increases because the inlet concentration term \(3-C_A\) initially dominates. The temperature also increases because heat generation \(3C_A^2\) adds energy to the reactor.
▶ MATLAB Code

MATLAB Code — P17 Non-Isothermal CSTR RK4 System

Coupled Concentration-Temperature ODE System
%% P17 — Non-Isothermal CSTR Start-Up using RK4
% Coupled ODE system:
%     dCA/dt = 3 - CA - 0.25*CA^2
%     dT/dt  = 440 - 1.4*T + 3*CA^2

clc;
clear;
close all;

h = 0.2;
t0 = 0;
tf = 1.0;

t = t0:h:tf;
N = length(t);

Y = zeros(2,N);

% Initial conditions:
% Y(1,:) = CA
% Y(2,:) = T

Y(:,1) = [1.0; 300.0];

% ODE function vector

f = @(t,Y) [ ...
    3 - Y(1) - 0.25*Y(1)^2; ...
    440 - 1.4*Y(2) + 3*Y(1)^2 ];

% Storage for RK4 slopes

K1 = zeros(2,N-1);
K2 = zeros(2,N-1);
K3 = zeros(2,N-1);
K4 = zeros(2,N-1);

for n = 1:N-1

    K1(:,n) = f(t(n), Y(:,n));

    K2(:,n) = f(t(n)+h/2, Y(:,n)+(h/2)*K1(:,n));

    K3(:,n) = f(t(n)+h/2, Y(:,n)+(h/2)*K2(:,n));

    K4(:,n) = f(t(n)+h, Y(:,n)+h*K3(:,n));

    Y(:,n+1) = Y(:,n) + (h/6)*(K1(:,n)+2*K2(:,n)+2*K3(:,n)+K4(:,n));

end

CA = Y(1,:)';
Temp = Y(2,:)';

Results = table(t', CA, Temp, ...
    'VariableNames', {'Time', 'CA', 'Temperature'});

disp(Results)

fprintf('CA(1.0) = %.6f\n', CA(end))
fprintf('T(1.0)  = %.6f\n', Temp(end))

figure;
plot(t, CA, '-o', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;
xlabel('Time');
ylabel('C_A');
title('Concentration Response in Non-Isothermal CSTR');

figure;
plot(t, Temp, '-s', 'LineWidth', 2);
grid on;
xlabel('Time');
ylabel('Temperature');
title('Temperature Response in Non-Isothermal CSTR');
